(9)  When a regulatory floodway has not been designated, the floodplain administrator must require that no new construction, substantial improvements, or other development (including fill) shall be permitted within zones A1-30 and AE on the community's FIRM, unless it is demonstrated that the cumulative effect of the proposed development, when combined with all other existing and anticipated development, will not increase the water surface elevation of the base flood more than one (1) foot at any point within the community. 
(10)  Under the provisions of 44 CFR Chapter 1, Section 65.12, of the National Flood Insurance Program regulations, a community may approve certain development in zones A1-30, AE, AH, on the community's FIRM which increases the water surface elevation of the base flood by more than one (1) foot, provided that the community first completes all the provisions required by Section 65.12. 
(c)  Permit procedures. 
(1)  Application for a development permit shall be presented to the floodplain administrator on forms furnished by him/her and may include, but not be limited to, plans in duplicate drawn to scale showing the location, dimensions, and elevation of proposed landscape alterations, existing and proposed structures, including the placement of manufactured homes, and the location of the foregoing in relation to areas of special flood hazard. Additionally, the following information is required: 
a.  Elevation (in relation to mean sea level), of the lowest floor (including basement) of all new and substantially improved structures; 
b.  Elevation in relation to mean sea level to which any nonresidential structure shall be floodproofed; 
c.  A certificate from a registered professional engineer or architect that the nonresidential floodproofed structure shall meet the floodproofing criteria of subsection4-4005(b)(2); 
d.  Description of the extent to which any watercourse or natural drainage will be altered or relocated as a result of proposed development. 
e.  Maintain a record of all such information in accordance with subsection 4-4004(b)(1). 
(2)  Approval or denial of a floodplain development permit by the floodplain administrator shall be based on all of the provisions of this chapter and the following relevant factors: 
a.  The danger to life and property due to flooding or erosion damage; 
b.  The susceptibility of the proposed facility and its contents to flood damage and the effect of such damage on the individual owner; 
c.  The danger that materials may be swept onto other lands to the injury of others; 
d.  The compatibility of the proposed use with existing and anticipated development; 
e.  The safety of access to the property in times of flood for ordinary and emergency vehicles; 
f.  The costs of providing governmental services during and after flood conditions including maintenance and repair of streets and bridges, and public utilities and facilities such as sewer, gas, electrical and water system; 
g.  The expected heights, velocity, duration, rate of rise and sediment transport of the floodwater and the effects of wave action, if applicable, expected at the site; 
h.  The necessity to the facility of a waterfront location where applicable; 
i.  The availability of alternative locations, not subject to flooding or erosion damage, for the proposed use. 
(d)  Variance procedures. 
(1)  The appeal board, as established by the community, shall hear and render judgement on requests for variances from the requirements of this chapter. 
(2)  The appeal board shall hear and render judgement on an appeal only when it is alleged there is an error in any requirement, decision, or determination made by the floodplain administrator in the enforcement or administration of this chapter. 
(3)  Any person or persons aggrieved by the decision of the appeal board may appeal such decision in the courts of competent jurisdiction. 
(4)  The floodplain administrator shall maintain a record of all actions involving an appeal and shall report variances to the Federal Emergency Management Agency upon request. 
(5)  Variances may be issued for the reconstruction, rehabilitation or restoration of structures listed on the National Register of Historic Places or the state inventory of historic places, without regard to the procedures set forth in the remainder of this chapter. 
(6)  Variances may be issued for new construction and substantial improvements to be erected on a lot of one-half (1/2) acre or less in size contiguous to and surrounded by lots with existing structures constructed below the base flood level, providing the relevant factors in subsection 4-4004(c)(2) have been fully considered. As the lot size increases beyond the one-half (1/2) acre, the technical justification required for issuing the variance increases. 
(7)  Upon consideration of the factors noted above and the intent of this chapter, the appeal board may attach such conditions to the granting of variances as it deems necessary to further the purpose and objectives of this chapter (subsection 4-4001(c). 
(8)  Variances shall not be issued within any designated floodway if any increase in flood levels during the base flood discharge would result. 
(9)  Variances maybe issued for the repair or rehabilitation of historic structures upon a determination that the proposed repair or rehabilitation will not preclude the structure's continued designation as a historic structure and the variance is the minimum necessary to preserve the historic character and design of the structure. 
(10)  Prerequisites for granting variances: 
a.  Variances shall only be issued upon a determination that the variance is the minimum necessary, considering the flood hazard, to afford relief. 
b.  Variances shall only be issued upon: 
1.  Showing a good and sufficient cause; 
2.  A determination that failure to grant the variance would result in exceptional hardship to the applicant; and 
3.  A determination that the granting of a variance will not result in increased flood heights, additional threats to public safety, extraordinary public expense, create nuisances, cause fraud on or victimization of the public, or conflict with existing local laws or ordinances. 
c.  Any application to which a variance is granted shall be given written notice that the structure will be permitted to be built with the lowest floor elevation below the base flood elevation, and that the cost of flood insurance will be commensurate with the increased risk resulting from the reduced lowest floor elevation. 
d.  Variances may be issued by a community for new construction and substantial improvements and for other development necessary for the conduct of a functionally dependent use provided that: 
1.  The criteria outlined in subsection 4-4004(d)(1) through (9) are met; 
2.  The structure or other development is protected by methods that minimize flood damages during the base flood and create no additional threats to public safety. 
(Ord. No. 4-2010, Art. 4, 6-1-10) 
Sec. 4-4005. - Provisions for flood hazard reduction. 
(a)  General standards. In all areas of special flood hazards the following provisions are required for all new construction and substantial improvements: 
(1)  All new construction or substantial improvements shall be designed (or modified) and adequately anchored to prevent flotation, collapse or lateral movement of the structure resulting from hydrodynamic and hydrostatic loads, including the effects of buoyancy; 
(2)  All new construction or substantial improvements shall be constructed by methods and practices that minimize flood damage; 
(3)  All new construction or substantial improvements shall be constructed with materials resistant to flood damage; 
(4)  All new construction or substantial improvements shall be constructed with electrical, heating, ventilation, plumbing, and air conditioning equipment and other service facilities that are designed and/or located so as to prevent water from entering or accumulating within the components during conditions of flooding. 
(5)  All new and replacement water supply systems shall be designed to minimize or eliminate infiltration of floodwaters into the system; 
(6)  New and replacement sanitary sewage systems shall be designed to minimize or eliminate infiltration of floodwaters into the system and discharge from the systems into floodwaters; and 
(7)  On-site waste disposal systems shall be located to avoid impairment to them or contamination from them during flooding. 
(b)  Specific standards. In all areas of special flood hazards where base flood elevation data has been provided as set forth in (i) 4-4003(b), (ii) 4-4004(b)(8), or (iii) 4-4005(c)(3), the following provisions are required: 
(1)  Residential construction. New construction and substantial improvement of any residential structure shall have the lowest floor (including basement), elevated to or above the base flood elevation. A registered professional engineer, architect, or land surveyor shall submit a certification to the floodplain administrator that the standard of this subsection as proposed in subsection 4-4004(c)(1)a., is satisfied. 
(2)  Nonresidential construction. New construction and substantial improvements of any commercial, industrial or other nonresidential structure shall either have the lowest floor (including basement) elevated to or above the base flood level or together with attendant utility and sanitary facilities, be designed so that below the base flood level the structure is watertight with walls substantially impermeable to the passage of water and with structural components having the capability of resisting hydrostatic and hydrodynamic loads and effects of buoyancy. A registered professional engineer or architect shall develop and/or review structural design, specifications, and plans for the construction, and shall certify that the design and methods of construction are in accordance with accepted standards of practice as outlined in this subsection. A record of such certification which includes the specific elevation (in relation to mean sea level) to which such structures are floodproofed shall be maintained by the floodplain administrator. 
(3)  Enclosures. New construction and substantial improvements, with fully-enclosed areas below the lowest floor that are usable solely for parking of vehicles, building access or storage in an area other than a basement and which are subject to flooding shall be designed to automatically equalize hydrostatic flood forces on exterior walls by allowing for the entry and exit of floodwaters. Designs for meeting this requirement must either be certified by a registered professional engineer or architect or meet or exceed the following minimum criteria: 
a.  A minimum of two (2) openings on separate walls having a total net area of not less than one square inch for every square foot of enclosed area subject to flooding shall be provided. 
b.  The bottom of all openings shall be no higher than one (1) foot above grade. 
c.  Openings may be equipped with screens, louvers, valves, or other coverings or devices provided that they permit the automatic entry and exit of floodwater. 
(4)  Manufactured homes. 
a.  Require that all manufactured homes to be placed within zone A on a community's FHBM or FIRM shall be installed using methods and practices which minimize flood damage. For the purposes of this requirement, manufactured homes must be elevated and anchored to resist flotation, collapse, or lateral movement. Methods of anchoring may include, but are not limited to, use of over-the-top or frame-ties-to-ground anchors. This requirement is in addition to applicable State and local anchoring requirements for resisting wind forces. 
b.  Require that manufactured homes that are placed or substantially improved within zones A1-30, AH, and AE on the community's FIRM on sites: 
1.  Outside of a manufactured home park or subdivision, 
2.  In a new manufactured home park or subdivision, 
3.  In an expansion to an existing manufactured home park or subdivision, or 
4.  In an exisiting manufactured home park or subdivision in which a manufactured home has incurred "substantial damage" as a result of a flood, be elevated on a permanent foundation such that the lowest floor of the manufactured home is elevated to or above the base flood elevation and be securely anchored to an adequately anchored foundation system to resist lotation, collapse, and lateral movement. 
c.  Require that manufactured homes be placed or substantially improved on sites in an existing manufactured home park or subdivision within zones A1-30, AH, and AE on the community's FIRM that are not subject to the provisions of paragraph (4) of this section be elevated so that either: 
1.  The lowest floor of the manufactured home is at or above the base flood elevation, or 
2.  The manufactured home chassis is supported by reinforced piers or other foundation elements of at least equivalent strength that are no less than thirty-six (36) inches in height above grade and be securely anchored to an adequately anchored foundation system to resist flotation, collapse, and lateral movement. 
(5)  Recreational vehicles. Require that recreational vehicles placed on sites with zones A1-30, AH, and AE on the community's FIRM either: 
a.  Be on the site for fewer than one hundred eighty (180) consecutive days, 
b.  Be fully licensed and ready for highway use, or 
c.  Meet the permit requirements of subsection 4-4004(c)(1), and the elevation and anchoring requirements for "manufactured homes" in paragraph (4) of this section. A recreational vehicle is ready for highway use if it is on its wheels or jacking system, is attached to the site only by quick-disconnect type utilities and security devices, and has no permanently attached additions. 
(c)  Standards for subdivision proposals. 
(1)  All subdivision proposals, including the placement of manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall be consistent with subsections 4-4001(b), (c), and (d) of this chapter. 
(2)  All proposals for the development of subdivisions, including the placement of manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall meet floodplain development permit requirements of subsections 4-4003(c), 4-4004(c), and the provisions of [section] 4-4005 of this chapter. 
(3)  Base flood elevation data shall be generated for subdivision proposals and other proposed development including the placement of manufactured home parks and subdivisions which is greater than fifty (50) lots or five (5) acres, whichever is lesser, if not otherwise provided pursuant to subsections 4-4003(b) or 4-4004(b)(8) of this chapter. 
(4)  All subdivision proposals, including the placement of manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall have adequate drainage provided to reduce exposure to flood hazards. 
(5)  All subdivision proposals, including the placement of manufactured home parks and subdivisions, shall have public utilities and facilities such as sewer, gas, electrical and water systems located and constructed to minimize or eliminate flood damage. 
(d)  Standards for areas of shallow flooding (AO/AH zones). Located within the areas of special flood hazard established in subsection 4-4003(b) are areas designated as shallow flooding. These areas have special flood hazards associated with flood depths of one (1) to three (3) feet where a clearly defined channel does not exist, where the path of flooding is unpredictable, and where velocity flow may be evident. Such flooding is characterized by ponding or sheet flow; therefore, the following provisions apply: 
(1)  All new construction and substantial improvements of residential structures have the lowest floor (including basement) elevated to or above the base flood elevation or the highest adjacent grade at least as high as the depth number specified in feet on the community's FIRM (at least two (2) feet if no depth number is specified.) 
(2)  All new construction and substantial improvements of nonresidential structures: 
a.  Have the lowest floor (including basement) elevated to or above base flood elevation or the highest adjacent grade at least as high as the depth number specified in feet on the community's FIRM (at least two (2) feet if no depth number is specified), or 
b.  Together with attendant utility and sanitary facilities be designed so that below the base specified flood depth in an AO zone, or below the base flood elevation in an AH zone, the structure is watertight with walls substantially impermeable to the passage of water and with structural components having the capability of resisting hydrostatic and hydrodynamic loads of effects of buoyancy. 
(3)  A registered professional engineer or architect shall submit a certification to the floodplain administrator that the standards of this section, as proposed in subsection 4-4004(c) are satisfied. 
(4)  Require within zones AH or AO adequate drainage paths around structures on slopes, to guide floodwaters around and away from proposed structures. 
(e)  Floodways. Floodways located within areas of special flood hazard established in subsection 4-4003(b) are areas designated as floodways. Since the floodway is an extremely hazardous area due to the velocity of floodwaters which carry debris, potential projectiles and erosion potential, the following provisions shall apply: 
(1)  Encroachments are prohibited, including fill, new construction, substantial improvements and other development within the adopted regulatory floodway unless it has been demonstrated through hydrologic and hydraulic analyses performed in accordance with standard engineering practice that the proposed encroachment would not result in any increase in flood levels within the community during the occurrence of the base flood discharge. 
(2)  If subsection 4-4005(e)(1), above, is satisfied, all new construction and substantial improvements shall comply with all applicable flood hazard reduction provisions of section 4-4005. 
(3)  Under the provisions of 44 CFR Chapter 1, Section 65.12, of the National Flood Insurance Program Regulations, a community may permit encroachments within the adopted regulatory floodway that would result in an increase in base flood elevations, provided that the community first completes all of the provisions required by Section 65.12. 
(f)  Severability. If any section, clause, sentence, or phrase of this chapter is held to be invalid or unconstitutional by any court of competent jurisdiction, then said holding shall in no way affect the validity of the remaining portions of this chapter. 
(g)  Penalties for noncompliance. No structure or land shall hereafter by constructed, located, extended, converted, or altered without full compliance with the terms of this chapter and other applicable regulations. Violation of the provisions of this chapter by failure to comply with any of its requirements (including violations of conditions and safeguards established in connection with conditions) shall constitute a misdemeanor. Any person who violates this chapter or fails to comply with any of its requirements shall upon conviction thereof be fined not more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) or imprisoned for not more than sixty (60) days, or both, for each violation. Each day the violation continues shall be deemed a new violation. In addition, the violator shall pay all costs and expenses involved in the case. Nothing herein contained shall prevent the Town of Amite City from taking such other lawful action as is necessary to prevent or remedy any violation. 
(Ord. No. 4-2010, Art. 5, 6-1-10) 
PART 5 - PUBLIC WORKS 
CHAPTER 1. - STREETS AND SIDEWALKS 
ARTICLE A. - OBSTRUCTING STREETS AND SIDEWALKS 

Section 5-1001. - Assembly on streets or sidewalks. 
    No persons shall assemble or remain assembled on the streets and sidewalks in sufficient numbers or in any manner as to constitute an obstruction to free passage thereon if requested to disperse by any officer of the town. 
Section 5-1002. - Hardware, furniture, merchandise or other works prohibited. 
    No person, firm or corporation, or its agent shall obstruct the streets, sidewalks or alleys of the town by placing thereon any hardware, furniture, merchandise, shelving, boxes or other works that will in any manner interfere with the use of the streets, sidewalks, or alleys by the public. 
Section 5-1003. - Sale of goods. 
    No person shall place for display for sale any goods, wares or merchandise of any kind upon any of the sidewalks of the town. No peddler or itinerant vendor shall sell or display for sale any goods, wares or merchandise of any kind on any public rights-of-way or any other public property within the town. All farmers and their employees will be exempt if selling products they grow, provided they have proper documentation. No permit will be required for farmers and their employees. 
(Ord. No. 1-2004, 2-3-04; Ord. No. 10-2004, 6-14-04) 
Section 5-1004. - Placing or leaving objects on streets and sidewalks. 
    No brick, stone or wood or other substances obstructing the free passage of persons and vehicles shall be placed or left to lie in any of the alleys, streets, or other routes of the town, nor shall any person place on or in any of the streets, sidewalks or alleys any boxes, crates, casks, or barrels of any description, or any other obstruction of any kind. Provided that any person erecting a building, may with town permission place building material for immediate use on the streets in such a way as not to interfere with the usual traffic. 
Section 5-1005. - Construction near sidewalk. 
    Before building or remodeling in close proximity to the sidewalk, a passage way shall be constructed so as to leave the sidewalk unobstructed and provide safe and easy passage. 
Section 5-1006. - Encroachments on streets. 
    It shall be the duty of the chief of police to notify all persons about to erect any building, sidewalk, wall or fence near the street or any public way or alley not to encroach upon the street or public alley, and if in the opinion of the mayor any obstruction is being, or has been, constructed on any street or public alley, the mayor shall cause a survey of the line of the street or alley to be made by a competent surveyor. If the survey shall show that the street or alley is obstructed by any building, sidewalk, wall or fence, the owner shall be required to pay the costs of the survey and shall be required to remove all obstructions at once. Every person who shall be found to have encroached on any street or public way or alley by any building, sidewalk, wall or fence and refuses or neglects to remove the encroachment upon notice from the chief of police within 10 days from the date thereof, shall, upon conviction, be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
Section 5-1007. - Construction of driveways and culverts. 
    No person shall construct or install any driveway or drainage culvert within the town without first receiving approval of the construction as to size and quality by the town authorities. 
Section 5-1008. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person violating any provision of this article, or any condition or regulation of a permit hereunder, shall be punished as provided in section 1-1008 and be subject to having any permits previously issued revoked. Each day that a violation continues shall be considered a separate violation. 
Section 5-1009. - Tables or chairs on public sidewalks. 
    Businesses requesting to place tables or chairs on public sidewalks immediately adjacent to such places of business shall apply for and receive approval from the town council before a permit can be issued to allow tables or chairs on public sidewalks. Each request will be reviewed individually by the town council before approval is granted. 
    Approval for businesses to place tables or chairs on public sidewalks must meet the following conditions: 
(1)  The town compliance officer shall inspect to assure public safety; and 
(2)  The business or owner requesting such must provide the town with satisfactory evidence of general liability insurance coverage naming the town as an additional insured in an amount not less than two hundred fifty thousand dollars ($250,000.00) with such insurance carriers acceptable to the town; and 
(3)  The tables or chairs must be placed during operating hours only; and 
(4)  The business or owner requesting such shall be responsible for the cleaning of all public sidewalks immediately adjacent to his place of business at such times and in a manner acceptable to the town compliance officer; and 
(5)  The tables or chairs must be used solely for food or beverage service; and 
(6)  Only furniture is allowed, specifically, tables and chairs designed and built to be used as restaurant furniture. 
    A permit allowing such use shall be issued only after approval by the town council. 
(Ord. No. 16-2011, 9-6-11) 
Section 5-1010. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE B. - USE AND CLEANLINESS OF STREETS AND SIDEWALKS 

Section 5-1011. - Use of nails and tacks restricted. 
    It is hereby declared unlawful for any person to drive any nails or tacks into the telephone, telegraph or electric light poles, or into any house or store situated on any sidewalk or street of the town, except with the prior permission of the owner. 
Section 5-1012. - Driving through street barricade. 
    No person shall drive any vehicle into or upon any alley or street that has been barricaded by an employee of the town. 
Section 5-1013. - Removing barricades forbidden. 
    No person, other than an employee of the town shall remove any barricade which has been erected by the town. 
Section 5-1014. - Burning trash. 
    It is unlawful for any person to burn any trash, garbage or substance on or in any public street, alley, park or public place within the limits of the town. 
Section 5-1015. - Advertisements. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to paste, post, nail or attach in any other manner any handbill, dodger, sign, card, placard or advertisement of any kind, business or political, to any pole, post or object on any public street, alley, sidewalk, or other public way; it shall further be unlawful to suspend or erect any banner, placard or advertisement of any kind over or across any public street, alley, sidewalk or other public way. 
(Ord. No. 494, 12-5-67, § 1) 
Section 5-1016. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person violating any provision of this article shall be punished as provided in section 1-1008. 
Sections 5-1017-5-1020. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE C. - EXCAVATIONS 

Section 5-1021. - Permit required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, except as provided by public utility franchises, or employees of the town in the course of their employment, to open, dig into, remove the surface from or excavate any street, sidewalk, alley, public way or place without first obtaining a permit therefor from the maintenance superintendent. 
Section 5-1022. - Application for permit. 
    The application for an excavation permit shall contain such information as required by the maintenance superintendent. 
Section 5-1023. - Regulations authorized. 
    In granting an excavation permit, reasonable regulations may be imposed including but not limited to: 
(1)  the manner of making the excavation. 
(2)  the location of the excavation. 
(3)  protection of underground utility installations. 
(4)  the duration of the excavation. 
(5)  required safety precautions, such as barricades, lights, warning devices, etc. 
(6)  the extent and size of the excavation. 
(7)  steps to be taken to protect nearby property owners. 
Section 5-1024. - Assets or insurance required. 
    The applicant for an excavation permit shall submit satisfactory evidence that he has sufficient assets or insurance to indemnify the town for any costs, losses or liabilities that it may incur by reason of the excavation, and to satisfy any judgments or liabilities arising out of the excavation. 
Section 5-1025. - Backfilling and resurfacing. 
    It shall be the duty of the person making any excavation hereunder to fill the excavation and restore the surface to a condition at least equal to the surface prior to the excavation. If required, the person making an excavation shall furnish a bond, deposit or other security sufficient to assure compliance with this section. Provided, however, that the town may elect to fill and resurface the excavation and charge the cost thereof against the person making the excavation. 
Section 5-1026. - Inspections required; fee. 
    All excavations except those backfilled and resurfaced by the town shall be inspected and approved by the town before and after backfilling and before and after resurfacing. A reasonable fee for each man hour or portion thereof spent by town employees making the inspections may be charged. 
Section 5-1027. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person violating any provision of this article, or any condition or regulation of a permit hereunder, shall be punished as provided in section 1-1008, and shall be subject to having his permit revoked. 
Sections 5-1028-5-1030. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE D. - STREET MAINTENANCE PROGRAM[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 10-2000, adopted July 11, 2000, did not specifically amend this Code; hence, inclusion of its provisions as Art. D, §§ 5-1031-5-1033 of Chapter 1 of Part 5 was at the discretion of the editor. 

Section 5-1031. - Public roads defined. 
    All roads or street in this state that are opened, laid out or appointed by virtue of any act of the legislature or by virtue of an order of any parish governing authority in any parish, or any municipal governing authority in a municipality, or which have been or are hereafter kept up, maintained or worked for a period of three (3) years by authority of any parish governing authority in its parish or by authority of any municipal governing authority in its municipality shall be public roads or streets as the case may be. 
(Ord. No. 10-2000, 7-11-00) 
Section 5-1032. - Acceptance of new streets into town street maintenance system. 
(a)  All new streets and bridges accepted into the town street maintenance system shall meet the following requirements: 
(1)  Street grades shall conform in general to the terrain and shall be designed to ensure proper drainage. 
(2)  Streets and bridges shall be in accordance with the state department of transportation minimum design standards. 
(3)  All streets, bridges and drain structures shall be constructed by the interested party to meet all requirements before acceptance by the city council. If a bridge is located on the street, it must be the same width as the street or wider. 
(4)  All new streets and bridges accepted into the town system must serve a public need. 
(5)  The city council shall not pay for or participate in any manner in the construction of such streets. 
(6)  There must be permanent rights-of-way on drainage laterals and any canals intersecting or leading to subdivisions. The width of the right-of-way for subdivision roads shall be a minimum of sixty (60) feet, with a minimum road width of twenty-four (24) feet. Rights-of-way for major roads shall be the minimum set by the state department of transportation and development. 
(b)  The following procedures must be accomplished in order to accept a street and/or subdivision into the town street maintenance system: 
(1)  The planning and zoning commission must recommend acceptance of the street into the system. 
(2)  The street superintendent shall inspect the street and/or subdivision and set a one-year maintenance period by the developer if it meets town specifications. 
(3)  At the time the street is accepted by the town, the developer must transfer to the town the mineral rights of the property in the street right-of-way. 
(4)  At the end of one year, the street superintendent shall inspect the street or subdivision and, if satisfactory, it will be presented to the city council and if approved, maintenance of the street or subdivision will be added to the town maintenance program. If the street or subdivision is not determined to be satisfactory by the street superintendent, the developer will be required to bring it up to town specifications before final acceptance. 
(Ord. No. 10-2000, 7-11-00) 
Section 5-1033. - Acceptance of existing streets into town street maintenance system. 
(a)  All existing streets and bridges accepted into the town system shall meet the following requirements: 
(1)  Property owners must furnish a right-of-way agreement. 
(2)  Required right-of-way: Sixty (60) feet minimum. 
(3)  Street must have at least two (2) property owners who reside on the road. 
(4)  Eighteen-foot roadway with two-foot shoulder making a total of twenty-two-foot roadway minimum width. 
(5)  Roadway may be gravel or asphalt but in suitable condition. 
(6)  All drainage structures to be in good condition and of proper size with roadway ditches in place where needed (driveways, drains, etc.) 
(7)  If a bridge is located on a street, it must be the same width or wider than the street. 
(8)  Bridges must be inspected by the street superintendent and found to be in good condition. 
(9)  Property owners to maintain street, drainage, drainage structures (bridges where applicable) for one (1) year after all requirements have been met. 
(b)  The following procedures must be accomplished in order to accept an existing street into the town street maintenance system: 
(1)  The planning and zoning commission must be notified upon acceptance of the street into the system. 
(2)  The street superintendent shall inspect the street and recommend the one-year maintenance period begin. 
(3)  At the end of the one-year period, the street superintendent shall inspect the street, and if satisfactory, recommend the street be accepted into the town street maintenance system by the city council. 
(Ord. No. 10-2000, 7-11-00) 
CHAPTER 2. - CEMETERIES 

Section 5-2001. - Rules and regulations. 
(a)  Generally. The following rules shall be observed in town cemeteries: 
(1)  For uniformity, all trees and shrubs will be furnished and maintained by the town. 
(2)  Individual plot owners are prohibited from planting trees, shrubs or plants. 
(3)  The cemetery maintenance supervisor has the authority to: 
a.  Remove any plants, shrubs, trees or tree stumps already existing that may be dangerous to visitors, undermine surrounding graves or interfere with proper execution of his job. 
b.  Remove very old crumbling material from falling copings and tombs. 
c.  Remove faded or dead arrangements or decorations, at his discretion or a maximum or two (2) times a year (before All Saints Day and before Easter). 
(4)  The Town of Amite City is not responsible for permanent or nonpermanent type vases or temporary markers. 
(5)  An interment fee will be charged and collected through City Hall to be placed in a designated cemetery fund for future beautification and maintenance. 
(6)  Persons committing vandalism and/or improper use of property will be fined one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) in city court. 
(b)  Maintenance, etc., of memorials and plots. Cleaning maintenance, repairs or straightening of memorials on individual plots is the responsibility of the owner and must conform to the rules of the town cemeteries: 
(1)  The owner of a plot or his contractor is responsible for disposing of any debris resulting from maintenance or repairs. 
(2)  No new coping or other borders are allowed except where already existing and in need of maintenance or repair. 
(3)  Maintenance of coping must conform to standards of the town cemeteries in design and color. 
(4)  Decorative pebbles, sand or similar coverings are not allowed except where already existing and in need of maintenance or repair. 
(c)  The rules and regulations to be followed by companies or persons doing work digging graves or erecting memorials in the town cemeteries shall be as follows: 
(1)  In sections for below-ground burial, each monument or marker shall be installed on a reinforced concrete foundation with finished concrete six (6) inches on all sides and at ground level a minimum of four (4) inches thick. 
(2)  In sections for above-ground burial in a concrete vault, a slab of reinforced concrete with a minimum thickness of six (6) inches shall cover the entire lot. When a burial vault of the bottom sealing type is used, the concrete slab shall extend at least one (1) inch above the seal. 
(3)  If the above-ground burial is to be in a vault constructed of marble or granite, the foundation requirements include twelve-inch footings of reinforced concrete, with twelve-and-five-eighths-inch reinforcement rods for a single vault and twenty-four-and-five-eighths-inch reinforcement rods for a double vault. 
(4)  In sections for above-ground burial in a concrete vault, the slab is to be poured by the town, at a cost of three hundred fifty dollars ($350.00) per grave space. This is in addition to the burial permit fee. The slab must be paid for when the lot is purchased, or with existing lot owners, before the burial takes place. 
(5)  The new part of Butler's Cemetery (Center) is designated as an above-ground burial area. 
(6)  The cemetery custodian is responsible for making sure grave space is in the proper location. 
(d)  Burial permit fees. 
(1)  Burial (interment) fees for all city cemeteries will be determined by the residence status of both the relative seeking the permit and the resident status of the deceased as follows. The fees apply to permits for all five (5) city cemeteries. 
a.  A resident of the Amite City Burial District requesting a permit for a resident of the Amite City Burial District (both of whom have resided in Amite for a minimum of five (5) of the last ten (10) years) ..... $ 50.00 
b.  A resident of the Amite City Burial District who has resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) years, seeking a permit for a non-Amite City Burial District resident who has resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) of the last ten (10) years ..... 100.00 
(Example: Person living in Amite seeking permit to bury relative living away from Amite for more than five (5) years.) 
c.  A non-resident of the Amite City Burial District seeking a permit for a resident of the Amite City Burial District whom has resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) of the last ten (10) years ..... 100.00 
(Example: Son or daughter living away whose parent or other relative resided in Amite.) 
d.  A resident of the Amite City Burial District who has resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) of the last ten (10) years, seeking to purchase a burial permit for a non-resident of the Amite City Burial District, who has not resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) of the last ten (10) years ..... 200.00 
e.  A non-resident of the Amite City Burial District seeking a permit to bury a non-resident of the Amite City Burial District, neither of who has resided in Amite for five (5) of the last ten (10) years ..... 300.00 
(Approval for purchase of above permit must be given by at least one (1) member of the council cemetery committee, who may elect to confer with one (1) or more members of the citizens cemetery committee.) 
(2)  Burial permits will not be sold to persons who do not already own an Amite City burial site unless they are eligible to purchase a site under conditions of site purchase as outlined in this section. 
(3)  Proof of lot/gravesite ownership will be: 
a.  A title deed (from the clerk of court's office), 
b.  A bill of sale from Amite City, 
c.  A will specifying the site has been passed down, 
d.  Or ability of person to locate the lot with headstones bearing the name or relatives/ancestors and proof of relationship to that person by the purchaser. 
(e)  Fee schedule for grave sites in Amite Memorial Gardens and Butler I and II. 
(1)  Lots in the Mulberry Street Cemetery and the Amite Cemetery (old) are sold only with special permission of the council cemetery committee. Pre-need gravesites/lots shall be limited to two (2) sites and may be purchased by a resident of the Amite City Burial District only. 
(2)  The sale of gravesites in the Amite City cemeteries are determined by the residence status of the person seeking to buy the site and the residence status of the person for whom the site is being purchased. 
a.  A resident of the Amite City Burial District seeking to purchase a gravesite for a resident of the Amite City Burial District must have proof of residence for both parties and both must have lived in the city limits for a minimum of five (5) years. 
Amite Memorial Gardens ..... $350.00 
Butler Cemetery ..... 300.00 
b.  A resident of the Amite City Burial District who has resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) years, for a non-resident of the Amite City Burial District who had resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) of the last ten (10) years. 
Amite Memorial Gardens ..... $450.00 
Butler Cemetery ..... 400.00 
c.  A non-resident of the Amite City Burial District seeking to purchase a gravesite for a resident of the Amite City Burial District who has resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) years. 
Amite Memorial Gardens ..... $450.00 
Butler Cemetery ..... 400.00 
d.  A resident of the Amite City Burial District who has resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) of the last ten (10) years, seeking to purchase a gravesite for a non-resident of the Amite City Burial District, who has not resided in the city for a minimum of five (5) of the last ten (10) years, may not purchase a gravesite without special permission of the cemetery committee, to be considered on an individual basis. Should permission be given, the costs are as listed below: 
Amite Memorial Gardens ..... $1,000.00 
Butler Cemetery ..... $950.00 
e.  A non-resident of the Amite City Burial District may not purchase a gravesite for a non-resident of the Amite City Burial District (neither of whom has resided in the city for five (5) of the last ten (10) years), except by special permission of the council cemetery committee. If approval is granted, the costs are as listed below: 
Amite Memorial Gardens ..... $1,500.00 
Butler Cemetery ..... 1,450.00 
(f)  Residents of the Amite City Burial District are defined as those who can show proof of residence with any of the following: voter registration cards, U.S. mail with street address, utility bills showing street address, drivers license showing street address. 
(g)  Residents of the Amite City Burial District include persons living within the corporate city limits of the Town of Amite City. 
(h)  Residents of the cemetery district, who do not reside in the city limits of the Town of Amite City, will pay an additional one hundred dollar ($100.00) fee for all categories of gravesites. 
(i)  There shall be an area set aside, as designated by the mayor or his authorized representative, in New Butler Cemetery and Amite Memorial Gardens to provide lots, at no cost, for the burial of still-born infants. One (1) of the infant's parents or one (1) grandparent of the infant must be a resident of the Amite City Burial District and provide proof of residence. There shall be no charge for the lot or the burial permit. 
(j)  There shall be an area set aside, as designated by the mayor or his authorized representative, in Amite Memorial Gardens and New Butler Cemetery to provide lots, at no cost, for pauper burials. The pauper must have resided in the Amite Burial District to qualify. There shall be no charge for the lot or the burial permit. 
(k)  There shall be an area set aside in Amite Memorial Gardens to provide for the construction of mausoleums and burial. The area set aside is Section 2, Row M. There shall be a charge for the burial permit, which provides for burial records and perpetual maintenance of the cemetery. 
(Ord. of 10-2-84; Ord. of 6-26-95; Ord. of 10-27-97; Ord. No. 16-2000, 6-6-00; Ord. No. 6-2001, 4-23-01; Ord. No. 15-2001, 11-6-01; Ord. No. 6-2003, 5-6-03; Ord. No. 7-2003, 5-6-03; Ord. No. 12-2005, 8-3-05; Ord. No. 7-2014, 6-3-14; Ord. No. 8-2014, 6-3-14) 
Editor's note- An ordinance adopted Oct. 2, 1984, §§ 1, 2, did not specifically amend the Code; hence, codification of the substantive provisions of the ordinance as § 5-2001 was at the discretion of the editor. 
CHAPTER 3. - TREES AND SHRUBBERY 
ARTICLE A. - GENERALLY 

Sections 5-3001-5-3020. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE B. - PUBLIC TREES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note- Ordinance No. 4-1989, adopted Aug. 15, 1989, did not specifically amend this Code; hence, inclusion of §§ 1-11 as Ch. 3, Art. B, §§ 5-3001-5-3031, was at the discretion of the editor. 
Cross reference- Streets and sidewalks, § 5-1001 et seq.; tress in cemeteries, § 5-2001(a)(i); parks and recreation, § 6-1001 et seq.; trees and shrubbery, § 5-3021 et seq. 

Section 5-3021. - Purpose and intent of article. 
    The purpose of this article is to define, regulate, and coordinate the planting of trees and shrubbery in the streets and public grounds within the town, to regulate the preservation, replacement and indiscriminate removal of trees on town property, and to establish procedures for fulfilling these purposes. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 1, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3022. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Drip line. A vertical line extending from the utmost portion of a tree canopy to the ground. 
    Forester. A person trained in forestry by the state forestry department, or equivalent. The forester shall have the authority and jurisdiction as granted in this article to regulate the planting, maintenance and removal of trees on streets and other publicly owned property to insure or preserve the aesthetics of such public areas. 
    Person. An individual, firm, association, partnership or corporation. 
    Public right-of-way. Any parcel of strip of land within the corporate limits of the town which has been dedicated to and accepted for public use and maintenance by the town, including streets and alleys. 
    Street tree. Trees, shrubs or bushes planted or growing on land lying within public rights-of-way. 
    Utility. Any publicly, privately or cooperatively owned line, facility or system for producing, transmitting, distributing, or collecting communications, power, electricity, heat, gas, water, sewage, storm drainage, oil products or other similar services and commodities. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 2, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3023. - Powers and authority of town. 
(a)  The town shall have full power and authority over all trees, plants and shrubs planted or hereafter planted in the streets, parks and public places within the corporate limits. The maintenance of such trees, plants and shrubs shall be subject to the provisions of this article. 
(b)  Such power and authority shall in no way be used with intent to restrict franchised utility companies from carrying out the terms of their franchise agreements, to pursue landscaping into areas in which it is not desired by the citizens of the town. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 3, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3024. - Advisory committee. 
(a)  Appointment; purpose. The mayor shall appoint an advisory committee on forestry which shall serve to advise the town on issues concerning public trees, planning, removal, planting and maintenance. The mayor shall consider recommendations from the council and interested civic organizations on the appointments of advisory committee members. 
(b)  Composition; removal of members. The advisory committee shall be composed of no less than three (3) persons and no more than five (5) who shall sit on such committee until removed by the mayor or until resignation. Failure to participate in committee meetings shall be just cause to be removed from such committee. The city council shall have input into the appointments horticulturist, one (1) forester, one (1) utility company representative, and one (1) contractor or developer. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 4, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3025. - Maintenance and removal of trees. 
(a)  Responsibility of town. The town or its appointed representative shall be responsible for maintenance of trees on public property. 
(b)  Written permission required for removal or destruction of trees and shrubs. Except as otherwise noted, any person desiring to remove or destroy any tree or shrub or public property shall first receive written permission from the town tree representatives, who shall follow the intentions and requirements of this article when considering the removal of trees. 
(c)  Public tree removal; replacement trees. Generally, public trees shall not be removed unless an imminent health and/or safety hazard is probable. Such threat shall be determined by the town's representative so appointed. 
    Removal of public trees in relation to construction or driveway building shall be indicated on subdivision plans and/or building plans submitted to the town for review. The town's tree representative or zoning board (whichever is reviewing the plans) can require that certain street trees be retained on public property if it appears that such trees will not have a significant negative affect upon such construction or development. Replacement trees must comply with the provisions of this article. 
    Developers and builders shall retain as many existing street trees as possible during construction projects. Where feasible, developers shall plant approved species of trees in public right-of-way, and replace trees removed on public right of way with trees at least three-inch caliper and at least eight (8) feet tall. 
(d)  Pruning techniques. When the town, any person or any business, is maintaining or cutting limbs on public trees, proper pruning techniques shall be followed; the minimum criteria for pruning of trees shall be as follows: 
(1)  In general, the best time to prune most trees is during late winter or early spring, before new growth appears (usually between March 1 and May 1). 
(2)  All final pruning cuts shall be made smooth and flush to the tree. Care should be taken not to leave a stub on a tree as this is an excellent port of entry for decay and fungi. 
(3)  Stub cutting of heavy limbs is recommended to prevent splitting the wood and stripping the bark. 
(e)  Removal of stumps. When trees are removed, the stump shall also be removed to ground level by the party responsible for cutting and/or removing the tree. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 5, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3026. - Planting of trees. 
(a)  Approval required. Before planting of any tree on town rights-of-way or town property, approval must be given in writing from the authorized representative of city hall. 
(b)  Approved tree list. New trees planted shall conform to the approved tree species list and shall take into consideration utility lines above and below ground on public rights-of-way. 
(c)  Placement of street trees. 
(1)  No street trees, other than those listed as small or medium sized trees, may be planted under or within ten (10) lateral feet from any overhead utility wire or directly over any underground water, sewer or transmission line. 
(2)  No street tree shall be planted closer than twenty (20) feet of any street corner (measured from the nearest intersecting curb or curb lines). No street tree shall be planted closer than ten (10) feet from a fire hydrant. 
(d)  Dead or deceased trees to be replaced. The town or its designated representative shall plant new street trees to replace dead or diseased trees at the discretion of the tree committee. 
(e)  Location of trees to be approved. Generally, location of new trees shall be approved by the tree committee. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 6, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3027. - Approved tree species list. 
    The following list constitutes those tree species that are acceptable as street trees. Small trees that are considered those growing no more than thirty (30) feet in height at maturity. Medium trees are considered those that grow no more than forty-five (45) feet in height at maturity. Large trees are those that grow to heights of over fifty (50) feet at maturity. 
Small Trees 
Dogwood 
Redbud 
Mayhaw 
Silverbell 
Sweetbay magnolia 
Magnolia soulangeana (oriental) 
Dahoon holly 
Wax myrtle 
Deciduous holly 
Cassina holly 
Cherry laurel 
Medium Trees 
American holly 
River birch 
Golden rain tree 
Sassafras 
Red cedar 
Blue beech 
Hophornbeam 
Tree palmetto 
Large Trees 
Sugar maple 
Tulip poplar 
Pin oak 
Shumard oak 
Water oak 
White oak 
Cedar elm 
American elm 
Small leaf elm (parvifolia) 
Thornless honey locust 
Ginkgo (male only) 
Red maple 
Southern magnolia 
Hickory Chinese elm 
Southern red oak 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 7, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3028. - Owners pruning of trees for corner clearance. 
    Every owner of any tree overhanging any street within the town shall prune the branches so that there is no obstruction of view for motorists at street intersections. The owner shall remove all dead, diseased or dangerous trees that constitute a menace to public safety. The town shall have the right to prune any tree or shrub, private or public, when such tree or shrub interferes with visibility along a street or obstructs a street light or traffic-control sign. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 8, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3029. - Attachment of devices to trees. 
    The town will not permit any person to attach signs, wires, chains or other devices which would be injurious to a tree. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 9, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3030. - Construction projects. 
    Where feasible, contractors, town crews and other persons working on public rights-of-way shall tunnel under major tree roots rather than using trenches, which sever the roots. Tunneling shall be used when placing underground utilities that interfere with existing street trees. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 10, 8-15-89) 
Section 5-3031. - Penalty for violations. 
(a)  Any person violating any provisions of this article or who shall fail to comply with any of the requirements hereof, shall be punishable by a fine not to exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00) for the first offense: and not to exceed five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each offense thereafter. 
(b)  In the event any person is dissatisfied with the decision of the authorized forester, that person may make a written appeal to the tree committee. The committee shall render its written opinion, affirming, overruling or modifying the decision of the respective agent as may be fit and proper under the existing circumstances. 
(c)  In the case where a provision of this article is found to be in conflict with a provision of any other ordinance or code in effect in the town, which established a lower standard for regulating and controlling the planting, maintenance, preservation, or removal of trees and shrubs, the provisions of this ordinance shall prevail, and such other ordinances or codes are hereby declared to be repealed to the extent that they may be found in conflict with this article. 
(Ord. No. 4-1989, § 11, 8-15-89) 
PART 6 - PARKS, RECREATION AND CULTURAL AFFAIRS 
CHAPTER 2. - RECREATION 
ARTICLE A. - GENERALLY 

Sections 6-2001-6-2020. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE B. - COMMUNITY CENTER[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 15-2000, adopted Nov. 14, 2000, amended Art. B of Chapter 2 of Part 6 in its entirety to read as herein set out. Prior to amendment, Art. B, §§ 6-2021-6-2023, pertained to similar subject matter and derived from Ord. No. 2-1999, adopted Jan. 5, 1999. 

Section 6-2021. - Use of center generally. 
    The following rules shall be observed when using the Community Center: 
(1)  Dancing is permitted at wedding receptions and private parties only. 
(2)  The Community Center is not available for concert or dances, however, church functions are allowed. 
(Ord. No. 15-2000, 11-14-00; Ord. No. 3-2009, 2-3-09) 
Section 6-2022. - Same-Charges. 
(a)  A deposit of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) is due at the time the reservation is made. The rental fee is due ten (10) working days before the event is held. 
(b)  The rental fee for a resident of Amite, with that person having an Amite ZIP code, is five hundred dollars ($500.00) per day. 
(c)  The rental fee for a nonresident of Amite, without having an Amite ZIP code is seven hundred dollars ($700.00) per day. 
(d)  The rental fee for an Amite-area non-profit organization, with an Amite ZIP code, is one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) per day. A copy of an IRS determination letter stating 501-C3 status must be attached to the contract if the applicant is a non-profit organization. 
(e)  Any Amite-area church can use the community center provided they have been established for five (5) years or more, have an Amite area physical address, have an Amite ZIP code, furnish the IRS determination letter stating 501-C3 status, pay a one hundred fifty dollar ($150.00) rental fee per day and a deposit of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) per day. 
(f)  The community center is available for rent by residents of Amite having an Amite ZIP [code] for private events that are held Monday through Thursday, such as birthday parties, showers, etc., for a maximum of two (2) hours for one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) per day. Each additional hour is seventy-five dollars ($75.00) per hour and includes the time that the air conditioning and/or heating system is operating and/or the resident is using the community center to decorate or prepare for the event. 
(g)  The community center is not available for rent for personal or business events that result in a profit, or that charge a fee for admission unless the renter is an Amite-area non-profit organization with an Amite physical address. A copy of an IRS determination letter stating 501-C3 status must be attached to the contract stating it is a non-profit organization. 
(h)  The community center is available for political events that do not result in fundraising activities for a fee of five hundred dollars ($500.00) per day and a deposit of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) per day. 
(i)  The community center is available for fundraisers for terminally-ill residents of Amite on a case-by-case basis, as determined by the mayor, for the same fees as an Amite non-profit organization with an Amite ZIP code. 
(j)  The renter is required to provide one (1) off-duty Amite Police Department officer at a rate of thirty dollars ($30.00) per hour per officer if alcohol is to be consumed at the event. 
(k)  If the use of the community center is not as stated in the contract, the deposit will be forfeited. 
(l)  A deposit of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00), plus the applicable rental fees, is due for each day the community center is rented. 
(m)  Cancellations must be made at least ten (10) working days in advance of the day of the rental or the deposit will be forfeited. 
(n)  Damage fees will be assessed according to the damage. 
(o)  A five dollar ($5.00) fee will be assessed if the community center key is not returned. 
(Ord. No. 15-2000, 11-14-00; Ord. No. 13-2007, 9-4-07; Ord. No. 3-2009, 2-3-09; Ord. No. 13-2014, 10-7-14) 
Section 6-2023. - Same-Other. 
(a)  Decorations may be applied with masking tape only to the walls and should be removed at the end of the event. No scotch tape, packing tape, or staples are allowed. 
(b)  There is not a P.A. system available. 
(c)  Each renter is responsible for setting up tables and chairs. 
(d)  The renter is to pick up the key to the Community Center the day of the event and return the same day. If city hall is not open, then the renter is to pick up and/or return the key to the Amite Police Department. A receipt for payment in full must be presented to receive the key. There will be no exceptions. 
(e)  The Community Center key will be given after 7:00 a.m. on the day of the event. Keys are not available earlier than 7:00 a.m. to ensure the facility is clean and available. 
(f)  If the Community Center is needed the day before the event for decorations, set up, or for any other reason, the renter must reserve the Community Center and pay a full-day rental fee. 
(g)  The deposit will be returned if the following guidelines are adhered to: 
(1)  All tables and chairs must be folded and returned to the storage area. 
(2)  The floor must be swept and mopped. 
(3)  All trash must be bagged and set in the garbage receptacles on the west side of the building. All trash on the outside grounds must be picked up. 
(4)  The lights and air conditioner and/or heating system are not to be turned on more than two (2) hours before the scheduled event and must be turned off before the building is locked. 
(5)  The Community Center keys must be returned on the day of the event. 
(6)  The Community Center and outside grounds will be inspected before the deposit is returned. If any of the above is not complete, the deposit will be forfeited. 
(Ord. No. 15-2000, 11-14-00; Ord. No. 13-2007, 9-4-07; Ord. No. 3-2009, 2-3-09) 
CHAPTER 3. - AMITE ARTS COUNCIL 

Section 6-3001. - Established. 
    The Amite Arts Council is hereby established as the agency specifically concerned with the arts and humanities in the Town of Amite. 
(Ord. No. 4-1999, 5-4-99) 
Section 6-3002. - Purpose; duties. 
(a)  The Amite Arts Council shall coordinate efforts to develop the arts and humanities and to formulate and implement goals for the cultural development of the Town of Amite City. 
(b)  The Amite Arts Council shall serve as advisor to the mayor and city council on arts and humanities related matters and cultural affairs. 
(c)  The Amite Arts Council shall serve as the coordinating agency among the city, parish, state and federal agencies and other agencies and institutions which provide and sustain cultural services in the community. 
(Ord. No. 4-1999, 5-4-99) 
Section 6-3003. - Membership. 
(a)  The Amite Arts Council shall serve, in accordance with policies and procedures developed by said Amite Arts Council, as the official arts agency for the Town of Amite City. In that capacity, the Amite Arts Council will make recommendations to the mayor and city council on available grants applications. 
(b)  The Amite Arts Council shall be comprised of eleven members. These members shall be appointed by the mayor and approved by a majority vote of the city council. All members shall serve a two-year term, with a term beginning date of July 1, 2002. Five members' terms shall terminate on June 30 of odd-numbered years and six members' terms shall terminate on June 30 of even-numbered years. 
(c)  The Amite Arts Council shall elect annually from its membership a chairperson, vice chairperson, and other such officers it deems appropriate. 
(d)  Vacancies shall be filled by appointment in the same manner as the original appointments. Appointments to fill unexpired terms shall be for the period of the unexpired term. 
(e)  Any member of the Amite Arts Council may be recalled at anytime by the city council for gross inefficiency, fraud, neglect, but only after an open hearing and upon notice specifying the complaint involved. 
(f)  All Amite Arts Council members shall serve without compensation, but shall be entitled to recover for any out of pocket expenses incurred individually in conducting business for the commission, subject to the approval of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 4-1999, 5-4-99; Ord. No. 1-2000, 1-4-00; Ord. No. 14-2000, 11-14-00; Ord. No. 18-2002, 12-3-02) 
Section 6-3004. - Authority to obtain services, accept donations, etc. 
    Subject to appropriations by the city council, services of compensated professionals may be retained by the Amite Arts Council. Donations, trusts, contributions and gifts may be accepted by the Amite Arts Council provided they are used to further the purpose for which it exists. 
(Ord. No. 4-1999, 5-4-99) 
Section 6-3005. - Funding. 
    Funding for the Amite Arts Council shall be twelve thousand dollars ($12,000.00) annually and shall be provided by those funds received as franchise fees from Spectrum, formerly Charter Communications LLC, provided that the town continues to receive franchise fees from Spectrum for cable operations. 
(Ord. No. 4-1999, 5-4-99; Ord. No. 3-2018, 3-6-18) 
CHAPTER 4. - AMITE SPORTS COMPLEX COMMISSION 

Section 6-4001. - Established. 
    The Amite Sports Complex Commission is hereby established as the agency specifically concerned with the development and operation of the T.W. Kent Sports Complex. 
(Ord. No. 10-2007, 7-3-07) 
Section 6-4002. - Purpose; duties. 
    The Amite Sports Complex Commission will oversee the development, construction and operation of the T.W. Kent Sports Complex. The commission will develop rules and regulations as well as maintenance and operational guidelines. 
(Ord. No. 10-2007, 7-3-07) 
Section 6-4003. - Membership. 
(a)  The Amite Sports Complex Commission shall serve, in accordance with policies and procedures developed by said Amite Sports Complex Commission, as the official sports complex agency for the Town of Amite City. In that capacity, the Amite Sports Complex Commission will make recommendations to the mayor and city council on operational activities, available funding, design, maintenance, fees, rules and regulations and other daily activities associated with operating the T.W. Kent Sports Complex. 
(b)  The Amite Sports Complex Commission shall be comprised of five (5) members. Two (2) of the members will be recommended by the T.W. Kent family, one (1) recommended by Amite Area Youth Sports Association, one (1) recommended by RAC and one (1) recommended by the Amite City Council. 
(c)  These members shall be appointed by the mayor and approved by a majority vote of the city council. All members shall serve a four-year term, with the first term beginning date of July 2007. 
(d)  Vacancies shall be filled by appointment in the same manner as the original appointments. Appointments to fill unexpired terms shall be for the period of the unexpired term. 
(e)  Any member of the Amite Sports Complex may be recalled at any time by the city council for gross inefficiency, fraud, neglect, but only after an open hearing and upon notice specifying the complaint involved. 
(f)  All Amite Sports Complex Commission members shall serve without compensation, but shall be entitled to recover any out-of-pocket expenses incurred individually in conducting business for the commission, subject to the approval of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 10-2007, 7-3-07) 
Section 6-4004. - Authority to obtain services, accept donations, etc. 
    Subject to appropriations by the city council, services of compensated professionals may be retained by the Amite Sports Complex Commission. Donations, trusts, contributions, and gifts may be accepted by the Amite Sports Complex Commission provided they are used to further the purpose for which it exists. 
(Ord. No. 10-2007, 7-3-07) 
CHAPTER 5. - PARKS 

Section 6-5001. - Park rules and regulations. 
    The Town of Amite City owns and operates Fleet Easley Memorial Park, Butler Park, Camille Street Park and Coach Catha Park. The following rules shall be observed when using the town's parks: 
(1)  Park hours are from dawn to dusk. 
(2)  No alcoholic beverages are allowed. 
(3)  No drugs of any type are allowed. 
(4)  No smoking on park premises. 
(5)  No three-wheeled vehicles, bicycles or motorized recreational vehicles are allowed. 
(6)  No loud music, loud noise, or profanity is allowed. 
(7)  No loitering is allowed. 
(8)  Anyone caught damaging or abusing the park, or any park equipment, will be charged and prosecuted to the fullest extent of the law. 
(9)  Violators may be banned from use of the park. 
(10)  Proper attire must be worn at all times. Shirts and shoes are required. No bathing suits and no sagging pants or sagging shorts will be allowed. 
(11)  Water slides, inflatables, bounce houses, jumpers and inflatable slides are not allowed. 
(12)  Open flames, propane gas burners, boiling pots, etc., are not allowed. Crawfish, shrimp and/or crab boiling is strictly prohibited. 
(13)  Any family or group function held at the park will require pre-approval from city hall. 
(Ord. No. 22-2009, 4-7-09; Ord. No. 11-2010, 8-3-10; Ord. No. 6-2014, 5-6-14; Ord. No. 8-2016, 6-7-16) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 22-2009, adopted April 7, 2009, did not specify manner of inclusion; hence, inclusion as pt. 6, chapter 5, § 6-5001 is at the discretion of the editor. 
Section 6-5002. - Amite Community Market use of Coach Catha Park. 
(a)  The Amite Community Market may use Coach Catha Park each Saturday of the year for the sole purpose of a community market displaying and selling homemade and homegrown items. Local vendors shall reserve and rent booth space directly from the Amite Community Market for the purpose of displaying and selling their wares. 
(b)  The rental fee is fifty dollars ($50.00), payable from the Amite Community Market to the Town of Amite City. 
(c)  The Amite Community Market will provide documentation from the Louisiana Secretary of State's office that they are in good standing. 
(d)  If the use of the Coach Catha Park is not as stated, permission to use is revoked. 
(e)  The rental fee is not due on any Saturday that the Amite Community Market is cancelled due to weather, disasters, or any other unforeseen emergency that would prevent it from being held. 
(f)  The following guidelines must be followed: 
(1)  No alcoholic beverages allowed in park. 
(2)  No three-wheelers or go-carts allowed in park. 
(3)  No loud music, loud noise, or profanity allowed in park. 
(4)  Anyone caught damaging or abusing park will be charged and prosecuted according to law. 
(Ord. No. 16-2014, 12-2-14)

Section 6-6001. - Established. 
    The Amite Fitness Council is hereby established as an agency specifically to promote and maintain health and wellness for the citizens of the Town of Amite City.

In that capacity, the Amite Fitness Council will make recommendations to the mayor and city council on activities, funding, rules and regulations and other activities associated with the fitness council. 
(b)  The Amite Fitness Council shall be comprised of nine (9) members. These members shall be appointed by the mayor and approved by a majority vote of the city council. All members shall serve a four-year term, with the first term beginning date of January 2013. 
(c)  Vacancies shall be filled by appointment in the same manner as the original appointments. Appointments to fill unexpired terms shall be the period of the unexpired term. 
(d)  Any member of the Amite Fitness Council may be recalled at any time by the city council for gross inefficiency, fraud, neglect, but only after an open hearing and upon notice specifying the complaint involved. 
(e)  All Amite Fitness Council members shall serve without compensation, but shall be entitled to recover any out-of-pocket expenses incurred individually in conducting business for the commission, subject to the approval of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 4-2013, 6-4-13)

    Subject to appropriations by the city council, services of compensated professionals may be retained by the Amite Fitness Council. Donations, trusts, contributions and gifts may be accepted by the Amite Fitness Council provided they are used to further the purpose for which it exists. 
(Ord. No. 4-2013, 6-4-13) 
CHAPTER 7. - PARADES 

Section 6-7001. - Parade permits. 
    No person or entity shall engage in, participate in, aid, form or start any parade, unless a parade permit is obtained from the Town of Amite City. 
    A person seeking issuance of a parade permit shall file an application with city hall on forms provided by the town not less than ten (10) days before the date on which it is proposed to conduct the parade. Said application must be approved by both the mayor and chief of police before such permit will be issued. 
    The application for a parade permit shall set forth the following information: 
(1)  The name, address and telephone number of the person seeking to conduct such parade. 
(2)  If the parade is proposed to be conducted for, on behalf of, or by an organization, the name, address and telephone number of the headquarters of the organization, and of the authorized and responsible heads of such organization. 
(3)  The name, address and telephone number of the person who will be the parade chairman and who will be responsible for its conduct. 
(4)  The date when the parade is to be conducted. 
(5)  The route to be traveled, the starting point and the termination point. 
(6)  The approximate number of persons who, and animals and vehicles which, will constitute such parade, the type of animals and description of the vehicles. 
(7)  The hours when such parade will start and terminate. A statement as to whether the parade will occupy all or only a portion of the width of the streets proposed to be traversed. 
(8)  The location by streets of any assembly areas for such parade. 
(9)  The time at which units of the parade will begin to assemble at any such assembly area or areas. 
(10)  The interval of space to be maintained between units of such parade. 
(11)  If the parade is designed to be held by, and on behalf of or for, any person other than the applicant, the applicant for such parade shall file a written communication from the person proposing to hold the parade, authorizing the applicant to apply for the permit on his behalf. 
(12)  Any additional information which the mayor and/or chief of police shall find reasonably necessary to a fair determination as to whether a permit should issue. 
    There shall be a fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for each parade permit. 
    The following shall not require a parade permit: 
Funeral processions. 
Students going to and from school classes. 
A governmental agency acting with the scope of its functions. 
    The mayor shall issue a parade permit when, from a consideration of the application and from such other information as may otherwise be obtained, he finds that: 
The conduct of the parade will not substantially interrupt the safe and orderly movement of other traffic contiguous to its route; 
The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so great a number of police officers of this municipality to properly police the line of movement and the areas contiguous thereto as to prevent normal police protection to this municipality; 
The conduct of such parade will not require the diversion of so great a number of ambulances as to prevent normal ambulance service to portions of this municipality other than that to be occupied by the proposed line of march and areas contiguous thereto; 
The concentration of persons, animals and vehicles at assembly points of the parade will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection of, or ambulance service to, areas contiguous to such assembly areas; 
The conduct of the parade will not interfere with the movement of firefighting equipment enroute to a fire; 
The conduct of the parade is not reasonably likely to cause injury to persons or property, to provoke disorderly conduct or create a disturbance; 
The parade is scheduled to move from its point of origin to its point of termination expeditiously and without unreasonable delays enroute; 
The parade is not to be held for the sole purpose of advertising any product, cause, goods or event and is not designed to be held purely for [to] provide profit. 
(Ord. No. 12-2013, 11-5-13) 
PART 7 - MUNICIPAL UTILITIES 
CHAPTER 1. - WATER SUPPLY AND DISTRIBUTION[1]
