(6)  [Counting of prior offenses.] For purposes of the progressive fines set forth in this section, prior offenses will be counted for a period of three (3) years from the date of the offense, and will not be counted after the lapse of three (3) years from the date of the offense. 
(7)  [Injunctive relief.] The Town of Amite City government shall also have the right to seek and obtain injunctive relief as may be deemed reasonable and necessary in order to prevent further violations of the water conservation restrictions set forth in this article. 
(8)  [When effective.] During the first full calendar month following the effective date of this article only, the fines and penalties set forth in this section hereinabove will not be in force and effect, but responsible parties will be issued warnings for violations of the provisions hereof in lieu of such fines and penalties. The fines and penalties set forth above will become effective on the first day of the month immediately following the first full calendar month after the effective date of this article. 
(9)  [Fines.] Fines imposed in accordance with this article shall be deemed to be civil fines and shall be charged to the responsible party. Fines will not appear on the responsible party's utility bills unless: 
a.  Fifteen (15) days have elapsed from the date of the citation and the responsible party has not filed an appeal; or 
b.  The appeals procedures have been exhausted and the fine is upheld. Where fines are assessed to city customers, such fines shall appear on such responsible party's regular monthly utility bill. 
Failure of a property owner to pay a fine on a utility bill will be treated as the nonpayment of a utility bill and may subject the property owner to disconnection of utility services. 
(10)  [Inspections.] Individuals designated by the street and water superintendent shall be authorized to conduct inspections of residential and commercial properties situated in the Town of Amite City in order to determine compliance with the provisions of this article and with any mandatory or voluntary water restrictions imposed under the authority thereof and to issue citations to property owners deemed to be in violation thereof. 
(Ord. No. 1-2008, 1-8-08) 
Sec. 7-3003. - Municipal addresses. 
    Each and every property holder shall number or have numbered with Arabic numbers not less than three (3) inches in height, every residential (single-family, multi-family, mobile home, or apartment complex), commercial or industrial building belonging to him/her in a visible location. The number will be assigned by city hall. 
    Water, sewer, and/or garbage service shall not commence until the property is properly numbered, as stated above. 
(Ord. No. 6-2012, 6-5-12) 
PART 8 - HEALTH AND SANITATION 
CHAPTER 1. - REFUSE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL 

Section 8-1001. - Collection of garbage. 
(a)  For the purpose of this chapter, "garbage" shall mean all putrescible wastes, including animal and vegetable matter and recognizable industrial by-products, but excluding sewage, human wastes, dirt and rocks. 
(b)  The town shall provide garbage collection service. Charges for the service shall be as established by the city council. Administrative rules and regulations may be promulgated by the city council as required. 
(c)  All residences within the city limits must pay a monthly charge for garbage collection. The charge for the collection of residential garbage within the city limits shall be nine dollars and seventy cents ($9.70). The cost for the collection of residential garbage outside the city limits shall be nineteen dollars and forty cents ($19.40). 
(d)  Commercial establishments inside the city limits shall pay the following monthly fee for garbage collection (charges are per can): 
Small Can: ..... $19.60 
Large Can: 
Once a week pickup ..... 39.60 
Everyday pickup ..... 55.25 
Multiple pickup - offices ..... 45.00 
Once a week pickup (with boxes/extra weight) ..... 55.25 
(e)  The town has the right to allow, on a case-by-case basis, commercial establishments to contract with an outside collection company when it is determined the town cannot provide services needed. 
(f)  Commercial garbage shall be collected from retail and commercial establishments as scheduled by the council. Garbage and litter shall be placed in containers not larger than 350-gallon capacity or in neat stacks at pickup points as established. 
(g)  Residential garbage shall be collected as scheduled by the council. Garbage and litter shall be placed in containers not larger than 90-gallon capacity or in neat stacks at the pickup point which shall be that point on the property nearest to the route of the garbage truck. 
(Ord. No. 13-1998, 9-1-98; Ord. No. 10-2005, 7-5-05; Ord. No. 3-2015, 5-5-15) 
Section 8-1002. - Bulky refuse. 
(a)  Contractors and/or property owners shall be responsible for the removal and disposal of all bulky refuse generated from tree trimming and tree removal activities and all bulky refuse from lot clearing and/or land clearing activities. 
(b)  Contractors and/or property owners are responsible for the removal of all bulky refuse generated from demolition, remodeling, and restoration projects. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for the contractor, property owner and/or lessee to place debris generated from demolition, remodeling or restoration projects on town right-of-way. 
(d)  The town shall provide for the collection of grass cuttings, leaves, limbs, branches, shrubs, and bushes of residential occupants that may be derived by typical landscaping or gardening projects, or generated by windstorm. Items must be stacked neatly on public right-of-way. 
(e)  Leaf piles and grass cuttings shall be segregated from limbs, branches, shrubs, and bushes. 
(f)  Items stacked shall not interfere with or block any roads, streets, avenues, etc. Items stacked on public rights-of-way shall not enter or cross the visible boundary of any public roadway within the town. Items shall not be placed in or over existing road ditches or any other drainage component. Items shall not obstruct access to any existing water meters, water shut-off valves, sewer connections, gas meters, garbage receptacles, fire hydrants, public parking areas, etc. 
(g)  Town employees or town equipment shall not enter onto private property. 
(h)  Items must be no longer than five (5) feet in length and three (3) inches in diameter in order that loading and transporting by town employees and town equipment can be done in a safe and practical manner. 
(i)  The street superintendent and/or his designated representative reserve the right to determine, on a case-by-case basis, if larger debris can be loaded and transported safely and practically. 
(j)  Emergency conditions may require the town to remove debris when such removal would protect the health and safety of the public. Emergency conditions include, but are not limited to, hurricanes, windstorms, ice storms, etc. 
(Ord. No. 2-1989, 2-7-89; Ord. No. 13-1998, 9-1-98; Ord. No. 10-2005, 7-5-05; Ord. No. 14-2005, 8-3-05; Ord. No. 3-2006, 6-6-06; Ord. No. 6-2009, 4-7-09) 
Section 8-1003. - Burial of refuse prohibited. 
    No trash, garbage, litter, construction and/or demolition debris, or any other material classified as solid or hazardous waste may be buried within the incorporated boundary of the town. 
(Ord. No. 5-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 8-1004. - Accumulation of refuse. 
    No person shall permit the accumulation of refuse and/or material classified as solid or hazardous waste on any premises, residential or commercial, within the incorporated boundary of the town. 
(Ord. No. 5-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 8-1005. - Interference with containers or contents. 
    No person shall interfere with city-approved garbage cans or containers or their contents except the owners or with the owner's permission. No garbage container shall be placed on city rights-of-way except those approved by authorized representatives of the town. All nonapproved containers will be picked up by the city trash collectors. 
(Ord. No. 2-1989, 2-7-89) 
Section 8-1006. - Trash burning. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to burn trash, garbage, refuse, or any material classified as solid or hazardous waste within the incorporated boundary of the town. 
(Ord. No. 5-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 8-1007. - Collection outside of town limits; fee. 
(a)  Levied. There is hereby levied a garbage collection fee of two (2) times the amount charged customers inside the corporate limits of the town per month for each person whose garbage is picked up and disposed of by the town, where the person resides or the business exists outside of the corporate limits of the town. 
(b)  Due date. The garbage collection fee shall be due and payable on the fifteenth day of each month; and that if the fee is not paid by the last day of any month the town shall cease to pick up the garbage for the person whose account is unpaid. 
(Ord. No. 428, §§ I, II, 10-4-55; Ord. No. 13-1998, 9-1-98; Ord. No. 10-2005, 7-5-05) 
Section 8-1008. - Outside garbage deposited inside city limits. 
(a)  It is unlawful for any person who does not pay a residential or commercial garbage collection charge to the town to deposit any waste, refuge, garbage, etc. in any residential or commercial containers located in or owned by the Town or to deposit trash, leaves, limbs or other debris inside the city limits. Violators are subject to a fine of up to five hundred dollars ($500.00) and/or sixty (60) days in jail or both. 
(b)  It is unlawful for an individual or business to deposit any waste, refuge, garbage, debris, trash, etc. in any commercial container not assigned to them. Violators are subject to a fine of up to five hundred dollars ($500.00) and/or sixty (60) days in jail or both. 
(c)  It is unlawful for any person to deposit any waste, refuge, garbage, debris, trash, appliances, etc. from outside the city limits inside the Town of Amite for trash disposal. 
(Ord. No. 5-1999, 8-3-99; Ord. No. 7-1999, 10-5-99) 
CHAPTER 2. - GRASS AND WEEDS 

Section 8-2001. - Control of weeds. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for persons owning or occupying lots or lot size tracts of land within the town to permit on lots or tracts weeds, grass, brush, or underbrush, growing or lying upon the area which has attained the height of twelve (12) inches or more, or to permit trash, rubbish, refuse, and debris thereof, and persons must maintain the lots or tracts free of weeds, grass, brush, underbrush, trash, rubbish, refuse and debris. 
(b)  When any premises within the town is not maintained in accordance with the provisions of (a) above, a written notice shall be directed to the person or persons owning or occupying the premises by the town, which notice shall require that the person owning or occupying the premises shall comply with the provisions of (a) above. 
(c)  Notices of violation shall be delivered to the person owning or occupying the premises a total of one (1) time during ownership or occupancy of premises. This notice shall constitute that said owner or occupant has been duly notified and is aware of any and all laws and/or ordinances that pertain to the control of weeds, grass, brush, trash, rubbish, refuse and debris growing or lying upon property. 
(d)  This notice shall be forwarded by certified mail, with a return receipt requested, addressed to the person owning or occupying the premises at his last known address. Notice directed to the person owning the premises as shown on the last assessment rolls shall be sufficient to constitute notice to the person actually owning the premises. 
(e)  The notice shall be presumed to have been received by the person owning or occupying the premises when deposited in the United State Post Office for delivery to that person. 
(f)  Upon failure, neglect or refusal of persons owning or occupying the premises to comply with the notice within ten (10) days after date of the written notice, provided the notice was properly addressed to the last known address of the person owning or occupying the premises, the person owning or occupying the premises shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished by a fine not to exceed five hundred dollars ($500.00) or by imprisonment for not more than sixty (60) days, or both such fine and imprisonment. 
(g)  In default of cutting, destroying, and/or removing from the designated areas all weeds, grass, brush or underbrush, trash, refuse, rubbish and debris growing or lying upon the area within the period provided for, the mayor or his duly authorized representative is hereby authorized and empowered, at the expense of the person owning the premises, to order by town forces or by contract, the cutting, destroying, and/or removing of the weeds, trash, brush or underbrush, rubbish, refuse and debris growing or lying upon the prohibited areas. 
(h)  If the cost or expense incurred by the town is not paid within ten (10) days, the clerk shall furnish the owner by certified mail a written statement showing the cost or expense incurred for the work. If the statement is not paid by the owner within ten (10) days thereafter, the amount thereof shall be included in and form part of the taxes due on the property. 
(i)  The clerk shall maintain a record of charges prior to the filing of the tax roll, the record shall be open to inspection at all times and shall constitute legal notice to the purchaser of the property, or parties lending money thereon, of the assessment. 
(Ord. No. 500, §§ I-VIII, 6-2-70; Ord. No. 11-2005, 7-5-05) 
CHAPTER 3. - DOGS, HORSES, COWS OR OTHER LIVESTOCK 

Section 8-3001. - Dogs, horses, cows or other livestock to be impounded. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any dog, horse, cow or other livestock to roam at large on any public street, alley, public playground or other public places in the town. 
(b)  Any dog, horse, cow or other livestock found roaming at large in violation of (a) above is subject to be impounded by the Tangipahoa Parish Animal Shelter, under authorization of the Tangipahoa Parish Code of Ordinances, Chapter 7, sections 7-1 through 7-94. 
(Ord. No. 454, §§ I-IV, 9-16-59; Ord. No. 15-1998, 9-1-98; Ord. No. 10-2002, 7-2-02) 
Sec. 8-3002. - Vicious dogs. 
(a)  [Definitions.] Definitions of terms as used in this section: 
(1)  Owner means any person, firm, corporation, organization or department possessing or harboring or having the care or custody of a dog. 
(2)  Vicious dog means: 
a.  Any dog with a known propensity, tendency or disposition to attack unprovoked, to cause injury to, or otherwise threaten the safety of human beings or domestic animals; or 
b.  Any dog which because of its size, physical nature, or vicious propensity is capable of inflicting serious physical harm or death to humans and which would constitute a danger to human life or property if it were not kept in the manner required by this section; or 
c.  Any dog which, without provocation, attacks or bites, or has attacked or bitten, a human being or domestic animal; or 
d.  Any dog owned or harbored primarily or in part for the purpose of dog fighting, or any dog trained for dog fighting. 
(3)  A vicious dog is "unconfined" if the dog is not securely confined indoors or confined in a securely enclosed and locked pen or structure upon the premises of the owner of the dog. The pen or structure must have secure sides and a secure top attached to the sides. If the pen or structure has no bottom secure to the sides, the sides must be embedded into the ground no less than one (1) foot. All such pens or structures must be adequately lighted and kept in a clean and sanitary condition. 
(b)  Confinement. The owner of a vicious dog shall not suffer or permit the dog to go unconfined. 
(c)  Leash and muzzle requirement. The owner of a vicious dog shall not suffer or permit the dog to go beyond the premises of the owner unless the dog is securely muzzled and restrained by a chain or leash, and under the physical restraint of a person. The muzzle shall be made in a manner which will not cause injury to the dog or interfere with its vision or respiration, but shall prevent it from biting any human or animal. 
(d)  Signs. The owner of a vicious dog shall display in a prominent place on his or her premises a clearly visible warning sign indicating that there is a vicious dog on the premises. A similar sign is required to be posted on the pen or kennel of the animal. 
(e)  Dog fighting. No person, firm, corporation, organization or department shall possess or harbor or maintain care or custody of any dog for the purpose of dog fighting, or train, torment, badger, bait or use any dog for the purpose of causing or encouraging the dog to attack human beings or domestic animals. 
(f)  Prohibitive locations. No vicious dogs shall be permitted in areas within three hundred (300) feet of any church, park or school within the limits of the Town of Amite. 
(g)  Insurance. Owners of vicious dogs after which declared vicious must within thirty (30) days provide proof to the city clerk of public liability insurance in the amount of at least fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00), insuring the owner for any personal injuries inflicted by his or her vicious dog. 
(h)  Penalties. Whoever violates any provisions of the section shall be guilty of a gross misdemeanor and shall be punished by a fine of not less than one hundred dollars ($100.00) and not more than five hundred dollars ($500.00), or imprisonment of not more than six (6) months in jail, or by both fine and imprisonment. 
(Ord. No. 12-2012, 8-7-12) 
CHAPTER 4. - JUNK 

Section 8-4001. - Vehicles; definitions. 
    As used in this chapter, the following terms shall have the respective meanings ascribed to them: 
(1)  Abandoned, stripped, wrecked or junked vehicles. Any motor vehicle which does not have lawfully affixed thereto both an unexpired license plate or plates and a valid motor vehicle safety inspection certificate, and the condition of which is one or more of the following: 
a.  Wrecked, 
b.  Dismantled, 
c.  Partially dismantled, 
d.  Inoperative, 
e.  Abandoned, 
f.  Discarded. 
Exceptions: The provisions hereof shall not apply to any motor vehicle in operable condition specifically adapted or constructed for racing or operation of privately owned drag strips or raceways; any motor vehicle retained by the owner for antique collection purposes rather than for salvage or for transportation; or any motor vehicle stored as the property of a member of the armed forces of the United States who is on active duty assignment. 
(2)  Owner. Any person legally vested with the title and ownership of any immovable property situated within the town. 
(3)  Vehicle. Any vehicle which was originally operable on two (2) or more wheels and which was originally capable of transporting one (1) or more persons. 
Section 8-4002. - Keeping prohibited; declared nuisance. 
    It is unlawful for any person to keep or deposit, or allow to be kept or deposited, abandoned, stripped, wrecked or junked vehicles on property situated within the town; and the presence of abandoned, stripped, wrecked, or junked vehicles is hereby declared to be a public nuisance. 
Section 8-4003. - Notice to remove. 
    In order to more effectively carry out the intent of section 8-4002, the town clerk shall send to the property owner as determined from the latest assessment rolls, or the occupant of the property, failing to comply with the requirements of this chapter, a written notice requiring the property owner to comply therewith within 15 days from the date of receipt thereof. The notice shall be posted by registered or certified mail, with return receipt requested. 
Section 8-4004. - Judicial determination. 
    If the owner or occupant of the premises so desires, he may, within the 10 day period after service of notice to abate the nuisance, request of the town clerk, either in person or in writing and without the requirement of bond, that a date and time be set when he may appear before the municipal court for a trial to determine whether he is in violation of this chapter, and whether or not the location and continued existence of the abandoned, stripped, wrecked, or junked vehicle on his property constitutes a public nuisance. 
Section 8-4005. - Failure to remove. 
    If there has been no compliance by the property owner or occupant with the requirements of this chapter within 15 days of a judgment of the court determining that he is in violation, the owner or occupant shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and on conviction thereof shall be punished as provided in section 1-1008 of this code. 
CHAPTER 5. - LITTER 

Section 8-5001. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this chapter the respective following terms and their derivations shall have the meanings ascribed to them: 
(1)  Authorized private receptacle. A litter storage and collection container constructed so to reasonably confine and retain litter and trash. 
(2)  Garbage. Putrescible animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking and consumption of food. 
(3)  Litter. Garbage, refuse, and rubbish, as defined herein, and all other waste material which, if thrown or deposited as herein prohibited, tends to create a danger to public health, safety and welfare. 
(4)  Park. A park, reservation, playground, beach, recreation center or any other public area in the town, owned or used by the town and its inhabitants, and devoted to active or passive recreation. 
(5)  Private premises. Any dwelling, house, building or other structure, designed or used wholly or in part for private residential purposes, whether inhabited or temporarily or continuously uninhabited or vacant, and shall include any yard, grounds, walk, driveway, porch, steps, vestibule or mailbox belonging or appurtenant to the dwelling, house, building or other structure. 
(6)  Public place. Any street, sidewalk, boulevard, alley, or other public way and any public park, square, space, grounds or building. 
(7)  Refuse. All putrescible and nonputrescible solid waste (except solid body waste), including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street cleanings, dead animals, abandoned motor vehicles and solid market and industrial wastes. 
(8)  Rubbish. Nonputrescible solid wastes consisting of both combustible and noncombustible wastes, such as paper, wrappings, cigarettes, cardboard, tin cans, yard clippings, leaves, wood, glass, bedding, crockery, plastic and similar materials. 
(9)  Vehicle. Every device in, upon, or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a highway, including devices used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. 
Section 8-5002. - Placing in receptacles; to prevent scattering. 
(a)  No person shall throw or deposit litter in or upon any street, sidewalk, or other public place within the town except in public receptacles, or in authorized receptacles for collection. 
(b)  Persons placing litter in public receptacles or in authorized private receptacles shall do so in such a manner as to prevent it from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any street, sidewalk or other public place or upon private property. 
Section 8-5003. - Sweeping litter into gutters; cleanliness of sidewalk. 
    No person shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street or other public place within the town the accumulation of litter from any building or lot or from any private or public sidewalk or driveway. Persons owning or occupying property shall keep the sidewalk in front of their premises free of litter. 
Section 8-5004. - Merchants' duty to keep sidewalks free of litter. 
    No person owning or occupying a place of business shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street or other public place within the town the accumulation of litter from any building or lot or from any public or private sidewalk or driveway. Persons owning or occupying places of business within the town shall keep all premises, including sidewalk, service alleys and parking area of their business, free of litter. 
Section 8-5005. - Litter thrown from vehicles. 
    No person, while a driver or passenger in a vehicle, shall throw or deposit litter upon any street or other public place within the town, or upon private property. 
Section 8-5006. - Truck loads causing litter. 
    No person shall drive or move any truck or other vehicle within the town unless such vehicle is so constructed or loaded as to prevent any load, contents or litter from being blown or deposited upon any street, alley or other public place. Nor shall any person drive or move any vehicle or truck within the town, the wheels or tires of which carry onto or deposit in any street, alley or other public place, mud, dirt, sticky substances, litter or foreign matter of any kind. 
Section 8-5007. - Litter in parks. 
    No person shall throw or deposit litter in any park within the town except in public receptacles and in such a manner that the litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any part of the park or upon any street or other public place. Where public receptacles are not provided, all litter shall be carried away from the park by the person responsible for its presence and properly disposed of elsewhere as provided herein. 
Section 8-5008. - Litter in lakes and fountains. 
    No person shall throw or deposit litter in any fountain, pond, lake, stream, ditch, canal, or any other body of water in a park or elsewhere within the town. 
Section 8-5009. - Litter on occupied private property. 
    No person shall throw or deposit litter on any occupied or unoccupied private property within the town whether owned by that person or not, except that the owner or person in control of private property may maintain authorized private receptacles for collection in such a manner that litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any street, sidewalk, or other public place or upon any private property. 
Section 8-5010. - Owner to maintain premises free of litter. 
    The owner or person in control of any private property shall at all times maintain the premises free of litter on any open or vacant private property within the town whether owned by that person or not. 
Section 8-5011. - Litter on vacant lots. 
    No person shall throw or deposit litter on any open or vacant private property within the town whether owned by that person or not. 
PART 9 - MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC 
CHAPTER 1. - GENERAL PROVISIONS 

Section 9-1001. - Highway regulatory act adopted. 
    Pursuant to the authority conferred by L.R.S. Title 32:41(c) the town adopts the provisions of L.R.S. Title 32, Chapter 1 (Louisiana Highway Regulatory Act), and all regulations of the state department of highways and the director of public safety adopted pursuant thereto, except for such provisions and regulations as by their nature can have no application in the town, and except as otherwise provided in this Code. 
(Ord. No. 502, § 1, 7-6-71) 
Section 9-1002. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person violating the provisions of the state highway regulatory act as amended shall upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-1008, provided that persons convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or narcotic drugs may be punished by a fine not to exceed five hundred dollars ($500.00) or imprisonment not exceeding sixty (60) days, or both. 
State Law reference- Municipal authority to impose penalties, L.R.S. 33:401(32). 
Section 9-1003. - Supervision, regulation, etc. by police chief generally. 
    The chief of police shall supervise and regulate all traffic on the public streets of the town; enforce the provisions of this chapter; investigate the public highways and effect methods and practices relative thereto as in his judgment and experience he deems advisable; and enforce them as an exercise of the police power of the town. 
Section 9-1004. - Making and enforcing regulations, permanent and temporary. 
    The chief of police is hereby empowered to make and enforce regulations necessary to make effective the provisions of this chapter and to make and enforce temporary regulations to cover emergencies and special conditions. 
Section 9-1005. - Authority to place signs, signals and markings. 
    The chief of police is authorized, and as to those signs and signals required herein, directed to place and maintain or cause to be placed and maintained all traffic signs and signals with the advice, consent and approval of the board. 
Section 9-1006. - Proof of insurance. 
(a)  The following words and phrases shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section: 
(1)  Motor vehicle means every vehicle which is self-propelled. 
(2)  Motorcycle means every motor vehicle having a seat or saddle for the use of the rider and designated to travel on not more than three (3) wheels in contact with the ground, but excluding a tractor and excluding a motorized bicycle. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a motor vehicle or motorcycle within the municipal limits without proof of insurance, as required by the provisions of Title 32 of the Louisiana Revised Statutes, present in the motor vehicle or motorcycle at the time of operation. 
(c)  Any person who violates this section shall be subject to a fine [of] not more than five hundred dollars ($500.00), and/or imprisonment of up to sixty (60) days. 
(Ord. No. 2-1996, § 1, 3-5-96) 
CHAPTER 2. - TRAFFIC REGULATIONS 

Section 9-2001. - Free flow of traffic; obstruction prohibited. 
    All persons are prohibited from engaging in driving procedures which obstruct the free flow of traffic in, around, over and through the streets, alley ways and other public ways of the town. Any person is prohibited from stopping his vehicle (except at a stop signal or stop sign, or to honor another driver's right of way, or in an emergency situation) in a manner as to obstruct the free and orderly flow of traffic by the maneuver, or to engage in unduly slow driving procedures so as to obstruct the free flow of traffic or to needlessly "circle the block" or dawdle, or make unnecessarily rapid accelerations and decelerations or to in any other manner constitute a traffic nuisance or hazard. 
Section 9-2002. - Speed limits established. 
(a)  No person shall operate any motor vehicle or tractor upon any of the streets and highways of the town at a greater speed than is reasonable and proper having regard to the width, traffic, and use thereof, or so as to endanger the property or life or limb of any person. 
(b)  The speed limits for the streets or portions of streets within the town are hereby established for those streets, or portions of streets listed in appendix I-A hereby incorporated herein. 
Section 9-2003. - Traffic signals at certain intersections. 
    Official traffic control signals shall be erected (or if heretofore erected are hereby ratified) at the intersections listed in appendix I-B hereby incorporated herein. Traffic at these designated intersections shall be directed by signals. 
Section 9-2004. - One-way streets established. 
    Upon those streets and parts of streets and in those alleys listed and described in appendix I-C hereby incorporated herein, vehicular traffic shall move only in the indicated direction when signs indicating the direction of traffic are erected and maintained at every intersection where movement in the opposite direction is prohibited. 
Section 9-2005. - Left and/or right turns prohibited at certain intersections. 
    It is unlawful for the operator of any motor vehicle, traveling upon the first-named highway at any of the intersections specified in appendix I-D hereby incorporated herein, in the direction or directions therein indicated in each case, to make a left turn and/or right turn at the intersection, as therein indicated. 
Section 9-2006. - Stop intersections established. 
    The intersections specified in appendix I-E hereby incorporated herein, are established as stop intersections, and official stop signs shall be erected (or are hereby confirmed if heretofore erected) in a position as to face traffic approaching the second-named street upon the first-named street, in the direction or directions therein indicated. All motor vehicles approaching the intersection upon the first-named street in the direction or directions therein indicated in each case, shall come to a full stop, within a reasonable distance, before entering the intersection. 
Section 9-2007. - Yield-right-of-way intersections established. 
    The intersections specified in appendix I-F hereby incorporated herein, are established as yield-right-of-way intersections and official yield signs shall be erected (or are hereby ratified if heretofore erected) in a position as to face traffic approaching the second-named street from the first-named street, in the direction or directions therein indicated. All vehicles and tractors approaching the intersection upon the first-named street, in the direction or directions therein indicated, shall yield the right-of-way to any motor vehicle in the intersection or approaching on the second-named street so closely as to constitute an immediate hazard during the time that the operator of the vehicle or tractor is moving across or within the intersection. 
Section 9-2008. - Vehicle weight limits established. 
    It is unlawful for any person to operate on any street of the town any motor vehicle, or other vehicle, tractor, trailer, or tractor-trailer combination, having an aggregate or gross weight equal to or greater than the weight specified for that vehicle in appendix I-G hereby incorporated herein, on the streets and/or highways or portions of streets and highways respectively described therein. 
Section 9-2009. - Tracked vehicles prohibited on streets. 
    It is unlawful for any person to operate any tracked or other vehicle having metal tracks or wheels upon the town streets. 
Section 9-2010. - Trains blocking crossings. 
(a)  It is unlawful for any person to operate or permit operation of any train, locomotive, or any other vehicle so as to obstruct, use or occupy any railroad crossings on any public street for more than fifteen (15) minutes at one (1) time. 
(b)  Any trainmen, conductor, brakeman, flagman or other member of the train crew or any other person in violation of this section shall upon conviction be punished as provided in section 1-1008. 
Section 9-2011. - Speed of trains. 
    It is unlawful for any person to operate a railroad train at a speed in excess of thirty-five (35) miles per hour within the town. 
Section 9-2012. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person who shall violate any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction be punished as provided in section 1-1008. 
Section 9-2013. - Left turns into angled parking spaces prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for the operator of any motor vehicle to make a left turn into any angled parking space on the city streets of the Town of Amite City. 
(Ord. No. 5-2005, 4-18-05) 
CHAPTER 3. - PARKING REGULATIONS 

Section 9-3001. - Vehicles to be parked within marked spaces. 
    Whenever a space is marked off on any highway for the parking of an individual vehicle, every vehicle there parked shall be parked within the lines bounding that space. 
Section 9-3002. - Parking prohibited at all times in certain locations. 
    It is unlawful for the owner or operator of any motor vehicle or other vehicle to park the vehicle in any of the places on the streets and alleys of the town specifically designated in appendix II-A hereby incorporated herein. 
Section 9-3003. - Parking prohibited in certain locations, certain days and hours. 
    It is unlawful for the owner or operator of any motor vehicle or other vehicle to park the vehicle in any of the places on the days and between hours indicated and specified in appendix II-B hereby incorporated herein. 
Section 9-3004. - Parking time limited in certain locations, certain days and hours. 
    It is unlawful for the owner or operator of any motor vehicle, or other vehicle to park the vehicle or allow the vehicle to remain parked in any of the places on the streets and alleys of the town, at any time on the days and between the hours indicated and specified in appendix II-C hereby incorporated herein. 
Section 9-3005. - Special purpose parking zones established, parking otherwise prohibited. 
    It is unlawful for the owner or operator of any motor vehicle, or other vehicle to park the vehicle or allow the vehicle to remain parked in any locations on the streets and alleys of the town established and designated as special purpose parking zones indicated and specified in appendix II-D, hereby incorporated herein. 
Section 9-3006. - Inoperative motor vehicles. 
    It is unlawful for any inoperative motor vehicle to be left standing on the streets, sidewalks, alleys or other town property for a period of more than twenty-four (24) hours. 
Section 9-3007. - Parking time limited; business establishments. 
(a)  The operator of any business establishment within the corporate limits of the town shall be allowed to exercise an option to prohibit motor vehicles from parking in front of his business establishment for more than two (2) hours; this option to be granted to the operator whether he owns or merely leases his business premises. 
(b)  When the operator of a business establishment wishes to exercise this option he shall notify the clerk and the necessary signs designating the space for the limited parking area shall be furnished by the town at the expense of the person wishing to exercise the option. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person to park an eighteen-wheeled vehicle in the downtown area of the Town of Amite City, unless said vehicle is temporarily stopped for the purpose of delivery or pickup of merchandise, packages, etc. 
(Ord. No. 455, §§ I, II, 10-8-59; Ord. No. 2-2007, 5-1-07) 
Section 9-3008. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person who shall violate any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction be punished as provided in section 1-1008. 
CHAPTER 5. - EMERGENCY VEHICLES 

Section 9-5001. - Approach of emergency vehicle. 
    Upon the approach of any police or fire department vehicle, or hospital ambulance, giving audible signal by an appropriate device, the driver of every other vehicle shall immediately drive to a position as near as possible and parallel to the right hand side of the street or highway, clear of any intersection, and shall stop and remain there, unless otherwise directed by police or traffic officer, until the police or fire department vehicle or hospital ambulance has passed. 
Section 9-5002. - Following and parking too near prohibited. 
    It is unlawful for the driver of a vehicle, other than one (1) on official business, to follow any fire apparatus traveling in response to a fire alarm, closer than five hundred (500) feet, or to drive and/or park the vehicle within the block, or within five hundred (500) feet of the place where the fire apparatus has stopped to answer a fire alarm. 
Section 9-5003. - Penalty for violation. 
    Any person who shall violate any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction thereof, be punished as provided in section 1-1008. 
CHAPTER 6. - ABANDONED, JUNKED, WRECKED OR USED MOTOR VEHICLES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Abandoned, stripped, wrecked or junked vehicles, § 8-4001 et seq. 

Section 9-6001. - Defined. 
(a)  As used in this chapter, the following terms shall have the respective meanings ascribed to them: 
(1)  Abandoned, stripped, wrecked or junked vehicles. Any motor vehicle which does not have a lawfully affixed thereto both an unexpired license plate or plates and a valid motor vehicle safety inspection sticker, and the condition of which is one (1) or more of the following: Wrecked, dismantled, partially dismantled, inoperative, or discarded. 
(2)  Owner. Any person legally vested with the title and ownership of any immovable property situated within the town. 
(3)  [Motor vehicle.] Any vehicle which was originally operable on two (2) or more wheels and which was originally capable of transporting one (1) or more persons. 
(4)  Department. The Amite Police Department. 
(b)  The provisions hereof shall not apply to any motor vehicle in operable condition specifically adapted or constructed for racing or operation on privately owned drag strips or raceways; any motor vehicle retained by the owner for antique collection purposes rather than for salvage or for transportation; or any motor vehicle stored as the property of a member of the armed forces of the United States who is on active duty assignment. 
(Ord. No. 4-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 9-6002. - Removal of abandoned vehicles, fees and charges. 
(a)  Any motor vehicles abandoned in or on the city street or city property for more than seventy-two (72) hours shall be removed and impounded. Nothing contained herein shall prohibit the department from removing and impounding any motor vehicle which is obstructing other traffic or the use of, on, over, to or from a public street or right-of-way. 
(b)  An abandoned vehicle impounded by the department shall be subject to towing charge and to a storage fee for each day it is impounded, commencing twenty four (24) hours after the vehicle has been removed to the pound. Such vehicles shall also be subject to a servicing charge. 
(c)  It shall be the responsibility of the owner of an abandoned vehicle to separately dispose of any violation charges in the appropriate court. 
(Ord. No. 4-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 9-6003. - Removal of junked, wrecked, or used motor vehicle; notice; sale. 
(a)  Any junked, wrecked or used motor vehicles located in or on the city street or city property shall be removed in accordance with the provisions of this section. 
(b)  The department shall place on a junked, wrecked or used motor vehicle ten (10) days before removal a notice that such vehicle shall be removed by the department from the city street or city property unless the owner of such vehicles removes it before the ten (10) days expire. Said notice shall be placed on such vehicle in a prominent place so that it is readily visible, shall state the date the ten (10) days will be expire, and state that any person having any interest in such vehicle shall contact the department before the expiration date. 
(c)  After the expiration of the time provided for above, the department shall remove such vehicle from said city streets or city property and tow or convey such vehicle to a scrap or junk dealer for purchase by said dealer as scrap or junk. Such vehicles shall be subject to a towing charge. 
(Ord. No. 4-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 9-6004. - Abandonment prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or deposit, or allow to be kept or deposited, or allow to remain a previously deposited, abandoned, stripped, wrecked or junked vehicle on property situated within the town; and the presence of any abandoned, stripped, wrecked, or junked vehicles is hereby declared to be a public nuisance. 
(b)  It shall also be unlawful for any person to abandon such a vehicle on private property within the corporate limits of the town or for such property to be located on any property with the exception of places of businesses and establishments that generally deal in the sale of such vehicles, their repair, maintenance and service, such as junk and scrap dealers, motor vehicle repair shops, service stations, and businesses dealing in the sale of such vehicles either at retail or wholesale. 
(c)  In connection with a junked, stripped, wrecked or inoperative motor vehicle located on private property, when such vehicle has been located on the property for a period of sixty (60) days, a letter by certified mail, return receipt requested, shall be directed to the owner or tenant of the property to remove the vehicle within ten (10) days from the receipt of the letter or if the owner or tenant is not available within ten (10) days from the posting of a notice on the vehicle as provided otherwise in this article, the department shall be authorized to seize and take possession of the junked, stripped, wrecked or inoperative motor vehicle and remove it from the premises on which it is located and dispose of it as otherwise provided in this article for such vehicles. 
(d)  The department shall furnish a monthly report in writing, containing the following information, to the directory of the motor vehicle division of the department of revenue of the state: 
(1)  Location of the junked or wrecked motor vehicle; 
(2)  All available identification information; and, 
(3)  Date of sale, and name and address of the scrap or junk dealer who purchased the junked vehicle. 
(e)  Any vehicle which remains on the public property or rights of way or private property after notice is given shall be considered public property and disposed of in accordance with this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 4-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 9-6005. - Sale of unclaimed abandoned vehicles. 
(a)  The department shall retain custody and possession of all abandoned motor vehicles removed to the pound for at least thirty (30) days from the date of impoundment, unless such vehicles are sooner released by the furnishing of bond, by legal process, or reclaimed by the owner upon payment of fees and charges as provided above. 
(b)  All vehicles remaining unclaimed in the pound for more than thirty (30) days shall be sold at auction or cash to the highest bidder after advertisement of such sale in the official journal one (1) time in ten (10) days. Delivery of the vehicle to the purchaser shall be made on the date of sale. The advertisement shall contain the following information: Make and type of motor vehicle, motor and chassis number (if any) and license number (if any). The advertisement may also contain the date of its removal and the place from where removed, and any other information reasonably describing such vehicle. The advertisement shall also state that the sale is without warranty either as to the title or mechanical condition. The vehicle shall not be sold unless the highest bid is sufficient to pay the cost of towing, storage and advertisement, and other costs arising from the removal, storage and sale. 
(Ord. No. 4-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 9-6006. - Procedure when no sufficient bid made at the sale. 
    If no bid for a vehicle, as provided in section 9-6004, is made sufficient to pay the costs provided above, the unclaimed abandoned motor vehicle shall be deemed a junked, wrecked or used motor vehicle and disposed of as provided in section 9-6003(c). 
(Ord. No. 4-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 9-6007. - Obligation of purchaser of auction sale of unclaimed abandoned vehicle. 
    The purchaser of the unclaimed abandoned vehicle at the auction sale shall remove the vehicle from the pound the date of the sale. In the event of failure to timely remove the purchased vehicle, the purchaser will be charged a storage fee for each day such vehicle remains in pound. 
(Ord. No. 4-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 9-6008. - Town employees prohibited from purchasing vehicles at auction sales of unclaimed abandoned vehicles. 
    No employee of the town shall purchase, directly, indirectly, through interposed parties, or other, any vehicle sold pursuant to the provisions of section 9-6004. 
(Ord. No. 4-2006, 6-6-06) 
Section 9-6009. - Records. 
(a)  The department shall keep a complete and accurate record of all abandoned, junked or unclaimed motor vehicles removed from the town street, town property or private property. The record shall contain the following information: 
(1)  Date of removal and impoundment of abandoned vehicles; 
(2)  Date or removal of junked vehicles; 
(3)  Place from which such vehicles were removed; 
(4)  Date of advertisement in official journal; 
(5)  Date of placing notice on such vehicles; 
(6)  Date of sale, and name and address of scrap or junk dealer who purchased as scrap or junk; 
(7)  Date of public auction of unclaimed abandoned vehicles and names of purchasers; 
(8)  All available identification information pertaining to such vehicles; and 
(9)  Any other pertinent information. 
(b)  The department shall also keep a complete and accurate record of all monies collected pursuant to or in connection with this article, including storage, towing, servicing and other such charges and fees, and sale prices. The record shall give details as to the date, the amount, the name of the person making such payment, and the name of the person handling the money for the department. Such records shall be at all times open to public inspection. 
(Ord. No. 4-2006, 6-6-06) 
PART 10 - LICENSING AND REGULATION 
CHAPTER 1. - IN GENERAL 

Section 10-1001. - Permit required to operate business or service establishment. 
    No person shall operate and conduct a business or service establishment, or any type of enterprise open to members of the public, prior to the issuance of a permit to him by the municipal authorities of the town, and which permit shall not be issued until a petition is presented to the authorities of the town, the petition to state the name of the owner, the exact location of the proposed establishment, the nature or the type of business and/or service to be conducted. 
Section 10-1002. - Permit required for use of town property for business operations. 
    No person or entity may enter upon, traverse, either above ground or below, or otherwise utilize any property, servitude, or other property right, owned, leased, possessed, or controlled by the town (herein referred to as "town property") for the conduct of business operations without first being issued a permit to enter town property for business operations as more fully set forth hereafter. 
    Permit application shall include an application fee of two hundred dollars ($200.00), plus one dollar ($1.00) per foot for each foot of town property the applicant's system will occupy. 
(1)  Location of any system for business operations within town property without a valid permit from the town pursuant to this section presents a threat to the health, safety, and welfare of the town's citizens and their property and is expressly forbidden. 
(2)  The town recognizes and reserves any and all rights available to it to regulate use of any town property. 
(3)  The granting of any town license, permit, or other requirement for doing business within the town shall not be construed as authorizing any such person or entity the right to utilize town property for the conduct of business operations. 
(4)  Any person or entity desiring to operate a system occupying town property ("applicant") shall make a written request to the town for a permit, which shall include the following information: 
a.  Name, address, telephone number, and contact person of the person or entity making the request; 
b.  Necessary corporate information, if applicable; 
c.  Name, address, email address, and home, office and cell telephone numbers of a person with authority to act on behalf of the applicant in case of emergency; 
d.  Description of the proposed activity; 
e.  Identification of the town property which applicant's system will occupy. Said identification shall include the following: 
1.  Map drawn to scale of the location of all of applicant's system presently occupying town property; 
2.  Inventory of all equipment, structures, and facilities comprising applicant's system occupying town property; and 
3.  Description of all anticipated construction, major maintenance, and major installation activities which shall include the specific locations, and the beginning and ending dates of all projects to be commenced during the next calendar year; and the tentative locations and beginning and ending dates for all projects contemplated for the two-year period following the next calendar year. 
f.  Proof of comprehensive general liability insurance covering and affecting the applicant's business operations occupying town property. Applicant shall notify the town of cancellation of such policy(ies) at least thirty (30) days in advance of such cancellation; and 
g.  Name of all contractors acting or working on behalf of applicant within town property along with the name and home, office, and cell telephone numbers of a person with authority to act on behalf of the contractor in case of emergency. 
(5)  Upon provision of all of the information required by section (d), the town shall issue a permit allowing the applicant/permittee to enter town property to conduct business operations in accordance with the specific information provided to the town by the applicant/permittee. 
(6)  Standard provisions of each permit granted pursuant to this section shall include the following: 
a.  Conditions of occupancy. The system shall be located so as to cause minimum interference with the public uses use of town property and with the rights and reasonable convenience of property owners who own property that adjoins town property. 
b.  Restoration of public ways. If, during the course of the permittee's construction, installation, or maintenance of the system, there occurs a disturbance of any town property by the permittee, the permittee shall replace and restore such town property to a condition reasonably comparable to the condition of the town property existing immediately prior to such disturbance. 
c.  Relocation at request of the town. If the town shall lawfully elect to vacate, relocate, abandon, alter, reconstruct or change any town property, the permittee, upon thirty (30) days' written notice by the town via certified mail to the permittee, shall remove, re-lay and relocate its structure, equipment, and facilities at its own expense. Should the permittee refuse or fail to remove system within thirty (30) days after written notification, the town shall have the right to remove the component parts of the system and charge the permittee for the costs of removal. 
d.  Relocation at request of third party. The permittee shall, on the request of any person holding a lawful building moving permit, protect, support, raise, lower, temporarily disconnect, relocate in or remove from any town property, as necessary, any property of the permittee provided: (i) the expense of such is paid by said person benefiting from the relocation, including, if required by the permittee, making such payment in advance; and (ii) the permittee is given reasonable advance written notice to prepare for such changes. For purposes of this section, "reasonable advance written notice" shall be no less than thirty (30) days in the event of a temporary relocation, and no less than one hundred twenty (120) days for a permanent relocation. 
e.  Interference with use of right-of-way. When working within town property, permittee shall not unreasonably interfere with public uses of said town property and the safety, health, and convenience of the public in the public's use thereof for ordinary travel. 
(7)  No less than three (3) business days prior to commencement of construction, installation or maintenance activities within town property, the permittee shall notify the town of the specific locations and beginning and ending dates of said construction, installation, or maintenance project and shall provide current, accurate contact information for both the permittee and the contractor as outlined in section (d). Upon receipt of this notification, the town shall determine whether the proposed construction, installation, or maintenance activities shall pose an unreasonable inference with public uses. If the town determines the proposed activity presents no such unreasonable interference, it shall issue the permittee a notice to proceed. If the permittee receives no written notification from the town within twenty-four (24) hours of the proposed commencement of activities, the proposed activities may be deemed approved. This section shall not apply to emergency repair projects or utility service extension projects which the permittee could not have anticipated. 
(8)  The permittee shall keep all of the information required by section (d) current at all times by immediately providing the town written notice of changes. 
(9)  Any person or entity (1) whose system occupies town property for business operations without obtaining the permit required in this section; (2) who fails to provide the 72-hour notice prior to commencement of construction, installation, or maintenance activities as required in section 6; or who fails to maintain current, accurate information required by section (f) concerning any system occupying town property may have any permit granted pursuant to this section revoked and may be denied future authorization for construction, installation, or maintenance activities for a period of two (2) years. 
(10)  Any violation of this section shall afford the town the full range of remedies available under any applicable law or regulation including the levying of fines. The election of one (1) or more remedies shall not be construed as a waiver of any other legal and/or equitable remedy including, but not limited to the town's right to seek injunctive relief, damages, and attorney's fees as the law might allow. 
(Ord. No. 24-2009, 6-2-09; Ord. No. 14-2012, 10-2-12) 
Sections 10-1003, 10-1004. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Former §§ 10-1003, 10-1004 were deleted as being superseded by the provisions of an ordinance adopted as presented Nov. 20, 1981. The deleted provisions pertained to an occupational license tax and derived from Ord. No. 402, §§ I, II, adopted Dec. 2, 1952. The new provisions pertaining to the same subject matter were codified as a new Ch. 5 of this part. 
Section 10-1005. - Retail dealers not having fixed place of business. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for the town or any officer or employee thereof to issue any occupational license to any person, firm or corporation which sells merchandise at retail and does not have a fixed place of business. 
(b)  This section shall include, by way of extension and not limitation, persons who sell from trucks or vehicles parked on or beside public streets and highways and persons who sell at temporary stands on or beside public streets or highways. 
(c)  This section is intended to exclude from the provisions of sections 10-1002 and 10-1003, the provisions of L.R.S. 47:369.1. 
(Ord. No. 401, §§ I-III, 11-5-52) 
Cross reference- Occupational license tax, §§ 10-5001-10-5006. 
Note- See the editor's note to §§ 10-1002-10-1004. 
Section 10-1006. - Foodhandlers permit. 
    The tax collector of the town shall demand of all persons, firms or corporations engaged in manufacturing, processing, distributing, serving, selling or offering for sale, prepared food, beverages, liquors, milk or milk products for human consumption, a written permit to be issued by the parish health unit to do business as required by the state sanitary code, before issuing them a town occupational license to do business in this town; provided if this is not issued or denied by the parish health unit within fifteen (15) days after application, the collector shall issue a license without the permit. If the permit is denied by the parish health unit, the collector shall not issue an occupational license until the permit is issued. 
(Ord. No. 415, § I, 11-14-54) 
Section 10-1007. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 27-2009, adopted June 2, 2009, repealed § 10-1007 in its entirety, which pertained to regulation of cable operators and derived from Ord. No. 2-1993, § 1, adopted Nov. 2, 1993. 
Section 10-1008. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 1-2005, adopted Feb. 1, 2005, repealed former § 10-1008 of the Code, which pertained to video draw poker devices and derived from Ord. No. 3-1994, § 1, adopted Nov. 29, 1994. 
Section 10-1009. - Electrical service permit. 
(a)  Permit required. 
(1)  It shall be unlawful for any public service company operating in the city to furnish electrical current to any building, tent, or structure or outdoor wiring of any kind, nature or description, without first obtaining a permit from the city. It shall be the responsibility of the customer to secure such permit and not the responsibility of the public service company. 
(2)  Subsection (a)(1) above shall not be construed to prohibit or restrict any public service company from repairing, extending or maintaining its lines, facilities, transformers, switches or other electrical devices and all such activity may be conducted without the securing of any permit of the city. Any new excavating requires a permit. 
(3)  The permit department of the city will not issue a permit for electrical services until after the appropriate deposits and fees for city services have been paid at city hall. 
(b)  Reconnection and upgrade service. A fee of ten dollars ($10.00) shall be paid for a reconnect and upgrade service to the city by each person requesting the permit for the commencement of electrical service. 
(c)  New construction. A fee of thirty dollars ($30.00) shall be paid for new construction requesting the permit for the commencement of electrical service. 
(d)  Penalty. Whoever violates any subsection of this section shall be fined not more than the sum of two hundred dollars ($200.00) for each violation hereof. 
(Ord. No. 11-2007, 4-3-07) 
Section 10-1010. - Regulating adult or juvenile residential care homes, independent living facilities and/or half-way houses. 
    No adult or juvenile residential care home or daytime care facility, independent living facility and/or half-way house providing housing and/or assistance to any substance abuser, mentally handicapped person, or person incarcerated or under the supervision of the criminal justice system shall be operated within the corporate limits of the Town of Amite City. 
(Ord. No. 14-2001, § 1, 9-11-01) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 14-2001, § 1, adopted Sept. 11, 2001, enacted new provisions which in effect superseded provisions formerly set out as § 10-1010 of the Code, which pertained to supervision of residents of adult or juvenile residential care homes, independent living facilities and/or half-way houses regulated and derived from Ord. No. 6-1998, adopted Feb. 3, 1998. The provisions of Ord. No. 14-2001, § 1, have been included herein as a new § 10-1010. 
CHAPTER 2. - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE CONTROL 

Section 10-2001. - Time of sale restricted. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to allow any saloon, bar room, bar or cocktail lounge to remain open between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m. on any day of the week or to remain open between the hours of 2:00 a.m. on Sundays and 6:00 a.m. on Mondays. 
(b)  Whosoever shall violate the provisions of this section by allowing any saloon, bar room, bar or cocktail lounge to remain open between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m. on any day of the week or between the hours of 2:00 a.m. on Sundays and 6:00 a.m. on Mondays, whether the person bet the owner, partner, manager, bartender, helper, employee or agent of the saloon, bar room, bar or cocktail lounge shall for each offense be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon trial and conviction thereof shall be punished as provided in Section 1-1008. 
(c)  Nothing in this section is to be construed to prevent any person from entering a saloon, bar room, bar or cocktail lounge between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m. or the hours from 2:00 a.m. Sundays until 6:00 a.m. Mondays for the purpose of cleaning or repairing the premises or for any emergency. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to sell, barter or trade any spirituous, vinous, or malt liquors containing more than one-half of one percent (1/2%) of alcohol between the hours of 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m. on any day in the town and it shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to sell, barter, or trade any spirituous, vinous or malt liquors, except beer and wine coolers, or any other beverage containing six percent (6%) or more of alcohol between the hours of 2:00 a.m. on Sundays and 6:00 a.m. on Mondays in the town. 
(Ord. No. 392, 2-9-51; Ord. No. 6-2004, 5-4-04; Ord. No. 8-2004, 6-14-04; Ord. No. 2-2011, 1-4-11) 
Section 10-2002. - Liquor permits. 
(a)  There shall be issued the following types of Class A retail liquor permits to businesses dealing in the sale of beverages of high alcoholic content of more than six (6) percent by volume. 
(1)  Class A-General: 
a.  A Class A-General retail permit shall be issued only to a retail outlet where beverage alcohol is sold on the premises for consumption on the premises by paying customers. Such an establishment must be equipped with a permanent wet bar equipped with a non-movable sink and a backbar or similar equipment for public display and to inform the public of brands and flavors offered for sale. 
b.  A Class A-General retail establishment shall be staffed by a bartender whose primary duty is to open and/or prepare beverage alcohol products for consumption on the premises by paying customers, or prepared with an appropriate lid or cover on the container for take out service. Such an establishment must meet all state and local health and zoning requirements as set forth by the state and by parishes and municipalities where a Class A-General retail outlet is located. 
c.  A Class A-General retail permit holder must derive at least seventy-five (75) percent of its total retail sales income from the sale of beverage alcohol for consumption on the premises. 
d.  A Class A-General retail permit shall be issued only to an establishment where the state law provides that no person under the age of eighteen (18) years is allowed on the premises except as provided in R.S. 26:90(A)(8)(a). 
e.  Notwithstanding the provisions of subparagraphs a. through d. of the paragraph, the permitting authority may issue a Class A-General liquor permit to any bona fide commercial film theater which had a Class A liquor permit on January 1, 1994. 
f.  Notwithstanding the provisions of subparagraphs a. through e. of this paragraph, the permitting authority may issue a Class A-General retail permit to any retail establishment for consumption on or off the premises. Such establishment must meet all state and local health and zoning requirements as set forth by the state and by parishes and municipalities where the retail outlet is located. A Class A-General retail permit issued pursuant to the authority by the subparagraph shall not be deemed or quality as a prerequisite for the issuance of any other type license or permit issued by the state or any political subdivisions thereof. 
(2)  Class A-Restaurant: A Class A-Restaurant permit shall be issued only to a "restaurant establishment" as defined in this paragraph and issued to a facility in conjunction with a Class "R" restaurant permit. A "restaurant establishment" shall be defined as an establishment: 
a.  Which operates a place of business whose purpose and primary function is to take orders for and serve food and food items; 
b.  Which serves alcoholic beverages in conjunction with meals; 
c.  Which serves food on all days of operation; 
d.  Which grosses sixty (60) percent of its average monthly revenue from the sale of food, food items, and non-alcoholic beverages; 
e.  Which maintains separate sales figures for alcoholic beverages; and 
f.  Which operates a fully equipped kitchen used for the preparation of uncooked foods for service and consumption of such foods on the premises. 
(b)  Fee schedule. Before engaging in the business of dealing in alcoholic beverages having an alcoholic content of more than six (6) percent alcohol by volume, all persons shall apply for and obtain from the tax collector of the town annually, with renewal on a twelve-month cycle from the date of the original permit, an annual permit to conduct each separate business located within the corporate limits of the town and shall pay for each permit according to the following schedule: 
(1)  Manufacturers, for each establishment: ..... $1,000.00 
(2)  Wholesalers, for each place of business: ..... 2,500.00 
(3)  Retail dealers: 
a.  Class A-General: 
Liquor permit fee for each place of business: ..... $300.00 
Beer permit fee: ..... $25.00 
b.  Class A-Restaurant: 
Liquor permit fee for each place of business: ..... 300.00 
Beer permit fee: ..... 25.00 
c.  Class B-Package: 
Liquor permit fee for each place of business: ..... 300.00 
Beer permit fee: ..... 25.00 
d.  A fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for each one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) of gross retail liquor sales, after the first one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) of gross retail liquor sales, shall be levied according to the schedule below, which shall be in addition to those fees levied in subsections (3)a. and (3)b. of this section: 
Gross Sales Additional 
Fees $0.00 to $99,999.99   0.00 100,000.00 to 199,999.99 100.00 200,000.00 to 299,999.99 200.00 300,000.00 to 399,999.99 300.00 400,000.00 to 499,999.99 400.00 500,000.00 to 599,999.99 500.00 600,000.00 and over 600.00  
(c)  Renewal permits. 
(1)  Failure to file application for renewal of permit not later than the month prior to the expiration date will incur the following penalties: 
Liquor: Five (5) percent of the permit fee with an additional five (5) percent for each additional thirty (30) days or fraction of thereafter if the dealer fails to make his application before the expiration date, his right to do business shall be suspended. 
Beer: Twenty-five (25) percent of permit fee. 
(2)  Renewal permits may be withheld and denied on the same grounds and in the same manner as an original permit. 
(Ord. No. 8-1996, 11-6-96; Ord. No. 2-2000, 1-4-00) 
Section 10-2003. - Beer permits. 
(a)  There shall be issued the following types of Class A retail beer permits to businesses dealing in alcoholic beverages having an alcoholic content of not more than six (6) percent by volume: 
(1)  Class A-General: 
a.  A Class A-General retail permit shall be issued only to a retail outlet where beverage alcohol is sold on the premises for consumption on the premises by paying customers. Such an establishment must be equipped with a backbar or similar equipment for public display and to inform the public of brands and flavors offered for sale. 
b.  A Class A-General retail establishment shall be staffed by a bartender whose primary duty is to open and/or prepare beverage alcohol products for consumption on the premises by paying customers, or prepared with an appropriate lid or cover on the container for take out service. Such an establishment must meet all state and local health and zoning requirements as set forth by the state and by parishes and municipalities where a Class A-General retail outlet is located. 
c.  A Class A-General retail permit holder must derive at least seventy-five (75) percent of its total retail sales income from the sale of beverage alcohol for consumption on the premises. 
d.  A Class A-General retail permit shall be issued only to an establishment where the state law provides that no person under the age of twenty-one (21) years is allowed on the premises except as provided in R.S. 26:90 (A)(8)(a). 
e.  Notwithstanding the provisions of subparagraphs a. through d. of this paragraph, the permitting authority may issue a Class A-General retail permit for beverages of low alcoholic content to a bona fide commercial film theater which had a retailers, Class A permit for beverages of low alcoholic content on January 1, 1994. 
f.  Notwithstanding the provisions of subparagraphs a. through e. of this paragraph, the permitting authority may issue a Class A-General retail permit for beverages of low alcoholic content to any retail establishment for consumption of beverages of low alcoholic content on or off the premises. Such establishment must meet all city and local health and zoning requirements as set forth by the state and by parishes and municipalities where the retail outlet is located. A Class A-General retail permit for beverage of low alcoholic content issued pursuant to the authority by this subparagraph shall not be deemed or qualify as a prerequisite for the issuance of any other type license or permit issued by the city or any political subdivisions. 
(2)  Class A-Restaurant: A Class A-Restaurant permit shall be issued only to a "restaurant establishment" as defined in this paragraph and issued to a facility in conjunction with a Class "R" restaurant permit. A "restaurant establishment" shall be defined as an establishment: 
a.  Which operates a place of business whose purpose and primary function is to take orders for and serve food and food items; 
b.  Which serves alcoholic beverages in conjunction with meals; 
c.  Which serves food on all days of operation; 
d.  Which grosses sixty (60) percent of its average monthly revenue from the sale of food, food items, and non-alcoholic beverages; 
e.  Which maintains separate sales figures for alcoholic beverages; and 
f.  Which operates a fully equipped kitchen used for the preparation of uncooked foods for service and consumption of such foods on the premises. 
(b)  Fee schedule. Before engaging in the business of dealing in alcoholic beverages having an alcoholic content of not more than six (6) percent alcohol by volume, all persons shall apply for and obtain from the tax collector of the town annually, with renewal on a twelve-month cycle from the date of the original permit, an annual permit to conduct each separate business located within the corporate limits of the town and shall pay for each permit according to the following schedule: 
Beer 
(1)  Wholesale dealers, per year (maximum $100.00) ..... $100.00 
(2)  Retail dealers: 
a.  Class A-General, per year (maximum $75.00): ..... 25.00 
b.  Class A-Restaurant, per year (maximum $75.00): ..... 25.00 
c.  Class B-Package, per year (maximum $60.00): ..... 25.00 
(Ord. No. 8-1996, 11-6-96; Ord. No. 2-2000, 1-4-00) 
CHAPTER 3 - INSURANCE COMPANIES 

Section 10-3001. - License tax-levy. 
    There is hereby imposed and levied an annual license tax on any insurer engaged in the business of issuing any form of insurance policy or contract, which may now or hereafter be subject to the payment of any license tax for state purposes, all as authorized by Section 1076 of Title 22 of the Louisiana Revised Statues of 1950 on risks located in this municipality as follows: 
(1)  On any insurer engaged in the business of issuing life or accident or health insurance policies or other forms of contracts or obligations covering such risks, or issuing endowment or annuity policies, or contracts, or other similar forms of contract obligations in consideration of the payment of a premium or other consideration for the issuance of such policies, contracts or obligations whether such insurer by operating in this state of through an agent or other representative or otherwise, ten dollars ($10.00) on gross annual premiums up to two thousand dollars ($2,000.00) and an additional license thereafter of seventy dollars ($70.00) on each ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00), or fraction thereof, of gross annual premiums in excess of two thousand dollars ($2,000.00). The maximum license on such businesses, payable to this municipality by any one insurer, shall not exceed twenty-one thousand dollars ($21,000.00). 
(2)  On any insurer engaged in the business of issuing policies, contracts or other forms of obligations covering the risk of fire, marine, transportation, surety, fidelity, indemnity, guaranty, workers' compensation, employers' liability, property damage, live stock, vehicle, automatic sprinkler, burglary, or insurance business of any other kind whatsoever in this state, whether such insurer is operating in this state through agents or other representative or otherwise, shall be as allowed by the aforementioned statutes, viz: 
1st Class: When the gross receipts are not more than two thousand dollars ($2,000.00), the license shall be forty dollars ($40.00). 
2nd Class: When the gross receipts are more than two thousand dollars ($2,000.00), and not more than four thousand dollars ($4,000.00), the license shall be sixty dollars ($60.00). 
3rd Class: When the gross receipts are more than four thousand dollars ($4,000.00), and not more than six thousand dollars ($6,000.00), the license shall be eighty dollars ($80.00). 
4th Class: When the gross receipts exceed six thousand dollars ($6,000.00), the additional license thereafter shall be seventy dollars ($70.00) for each ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00), or fraction thereof, in excess of six thousand dollars ($6,000.00). 
    The maximum license tax on such businesses, payable to this municipality by any insurer, shall not exceed the maximum limit of nine thousand dollars ($9,000.00), as provided for by L.R.S. 22:1076, above referred to; provided, that plate glass and steam boiler inspection insurers shall pay only one-third ( 1/3 ) of the above rates provided in said subsection (2); and provided further, that the amount of license payable to this municipality as fixed by this section, shall be one-third ( 1/3 ) of the amount so fixed if the payer shall file a sworn statement with the annual report required by L.R.S. Title 22, Chapter 1, Part XXIII, showing that at least one-sixth ( 1/6 ) of the total admitted assets of the payer, less assets in an amount equal to the reserves on its policies issued in foreign countries in which it is authorized to do business and which countries require an investment therein as a condition of doing business, is invested and maintained, either in bonds of the state, or in bonds of municipal, school, road, or levee district, or other political subdivisions of this state or in mortgages on property located in this state, or in real property in this state which shall be requisite for the convenient accommodation of the transaction of its own business, or in policy loans, or other loans to residents of this state, or to corporations organized under the laws of this state and domiciled in this state, or in stock of homestead building or loan associations organized under the laws of this state, to the extent such stock is guaranteed or insured by the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation or other federal or state agency. 
(Ord. No. 7-1996, § 1, 10-1-96) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 7-1996, adopted Oct. 1, 1996, enacted new provisions relative to insurance company license taxes which in effect superseded provisions formerly set out as §§ 10-3001-10-3003 of the Code, which pertained to similar subject matter and derived from Ord. No. 439, §§ 1, 2, 4, 5, adopted Sept. 3, 1957. 
State Law reference- Power of municipality to tax insurance business, L.R.S. 22:1076. 
Section 10-3002. - Same-Payment; delinquency. 
    All license taxes levied herein shall be due and payable on January first of each year and all unpaid license taxes shall become delinquent on March first. The collection of delinquent accounts shall be enforced in accordance with L.R.S. 47:1601 and 47:1602. 
(Ord. No. 7-1996, § 2, 10-1-96) 
Note- See the editor's note following § 10-3001.
